In this battle, dozens of bandits were killed, and government troops also suffered some casualties. Currently, Xiang Hanping is still concerned that the remaining bandits are lurking on the border and has agreed with the headquarters to leave Wu's regiment in Dongjiang awaiting orders. Wu's regiment departed from Shixing in Beijiang on the 3rd to return to the province and transfer to Dongjiang. Yan Yingyu's regiment will fill the defense of Shixing. (February 6)

Reasons for the Decline of Commerce in Shenyang

▲The Impact of Money Shortage and Gold Inflation

▲More Than a Thousand Stores Close Down

▲Government Agencies Prepare Relief Measures

Shenyang Correspondence: In recent years, all construction projects in Shenyang have made significant progress. However, the commercial sector has been in a state of depression and hardship, reaching its extreme. The main reasons are nothing more than the money shortage and the gold inflation. The market and commercial firms have been affected by this, leading to frequent closures. According to statistics from the Chamber of Commerce, there are approximately 15,000 commercial firms in Shenyang, and more than 1,000 have closed down this year, which is indeed a major problem in the Northeast today. Generally speaking, the standard of living in the Northeast is higher than that in the interior. In previous years, rising prices did not hinder merchants. This year, prices of various goods have fallen sharply, but there are fewer customers, so the commercial downturn of recent years is particularly severe this year. The so-called money shortage has become a common phrase among merchants, and the culprit behind the money shortage is the Feng Piao (Feng Tiao, Feng Currency). The Feng Piao's shortage is partly due to the government's unlimited issuance and partly due to the manipulation of unscrupulous Japanese merchants. When the Feng Piao was first issued, it was fully convertible without any loss. The so-called small silver coupons, which were valued at twelve jiao for one silver dollar, were relatively convenient for merchants to circulate. Later, the Japanese secretly manipulated, deliberately collecting Feng Piao from the market with silver dollars and exchanging them for silver dollars at the official silver bank, repeatedly causing chaos. (At that time, the Feng Piao gradually had a discount.) Over time, the value fell. The official silver bank, fearing that it would be unable to handle the situation if it continued, then issued silver dollar notes, which were not allowed to be cashed, for circulation in the market. However, Shanghai, Wuhan, Tianjin, and Jinan could be used for remittances to prevent fraudulent withdrawals. However, the number of issues was unlimited, and the value fell sharply. As of now, the authorities have stipulated that each Feng Piao is equivalent to one silver dollar, and the price has stabilized. However, 70% of the merchants have been ruined by this, so the older the brand, the greater the loss. As for gold inflation, it is not unique to the Eastern Provinces; all provinces have been affected. However, merchants in the Eastern Provinces have special circumstances. When the Feng Piao was falling, the Japanese used large sums of gold (the old-fashioned Korean currency, called gold notes by Shenyang merchants) to lend to farmers and merchants in the Eastern Provinces. The interest rate ranged from eight li to a maximum of one fen and two li, with most being one fen. The total amount reached 160 million yuan, with Shenyang alone reaching 80 million yuan. After the gold inflation, the gold notes also soared. Within a year, the exchange rate rose from one yuan and a few jiao in silver dollars for one yuan in gold notes to more than two yuan. Therefore, merchants who borrowed Japanese gold suffered heavy losses, and the financial situation in Shenyang was on the verge of bankruptcy. The Shenyang General Chamber of Commerce has repeatedly requested the authorities to find ways to provide relief to maintain the market. In the winter of 1929, the official silver bank of the Eastern Provinces had the intention of issuing silver dollar exchange coupons to restore the silver standard and maintain the market. However, it feared that the preparations would be insufficient, leading to the same mistakes as with the Feng Piao, so it hesitated to issue them. Currently, the money market is becoming increasingly scarce. After repeated requests from the Chamber of Commerce and after review by the authorities, it was deemed necessary to issue them. Recently, the official silver bank reissued 20 million exchange coupons, which are used in silver dollars without any discount. Since their circulation, the market has shown some activity. However, Shenyang's commerce has long been in a critical situation, and the lack of cash has reached its peak. The provincial government, recognizing this, has taken measures to maintain the prosperity of the provincial capital, including providing commercial and industrial loans. The method is for the government to order the official silver bank to provide 1.5 million yuan in cash to the Chamber of Commerce to establish a commercial and industrial loan office, which will lend to merchants in Shenyang at an interest rate of one fen and five li. The office is attached to the Chamber of Commerce and began accepting applications on the 1st of this month. Commercial firms that wish to borrow must first apply there, stating the name of the firm, the amount of the loan, the names of the shareholders, the names of the executives, the amount of capital, and the location. They must also have sufficient collateral and two guarantor firms. After the office completes the investigation and review, it can formally issue the loan. Since applications began on the 1st, 170 firms have applied as of the evening of the 4th, requesting loans of approximately 400,000 yuan. It is planned that the Chamber of Commerce will convene a board meeting on the 5th to review the applications of the firms to determine whether they are sound and whether the collateral is sufficient. After the review, the first batch of loans will be issued. However, the amount of loans is somewhat limited. For example, with 10,000 yuan of collateral, only 3,000 yuan can be borrowed. The maximum amount is 3,000 yuan. With 20,000 yuan of collateral, only 3,000 yuan can be borrowed. The cash is still stored in the official silver bank, and the General Chamber of Commerce only acts as an intermediary. The government's intention is to maintain the market and financial situation and to resist the input and manipulation of foreign capital. (4th)

Transfer of Jurisdiction in the Harbin Official Murder Case

▲Northeast Political Affairs Committee Orders Shenyang Court to Hear the Case

Harbin Correspondence: At 9:00 AM on the 6th, the Binjiang District Court received an order from the Northeast Branch of the Liaoning High Court, forwarded by the Northeast Political Affairs Committee, instructing that the case of Ye Yixiong, a judge of the Special District Court, murdering Zhang Wang Liqing, the female owner of the Xie Xing Sauce Garden, be transferred to the Shenyang District Court for retrial. According to the procedure, the Shenyang District Court Prosecutor's Office will first investigate and then file a lawsuit with the same-level court. Last night, the court assigned four judicial police officers to escort the files and Ye Yixiong to Liaoning. However, the transfer did not take place because the official transfer documents and all procedures had not been completed. It is scheduled to depart at 10:45 PM tonight. Last night, Ye's wife, Peng Churu, visited her husband at the detention center twice, bringing clothes and money. The couple met, hugged each other, and cried. The fellow inmates were all moved to tears. Ye, feeling that he had brought it upon himself, expected that there would be no good outcome after the transfer to Liaoning and repeatedly called out to his wife, "I'm sorry, I'm ashamed." However, the Binjiang Court originally intended to handle this case and did not dare to be negligent. After the first public trial on the 19th of last month, it was delayed for many days due to the illness of Judge Jia Jingyang. On the 3rd of this month, Jia returned to work after recovering from his illness and summoned Zhang Wang Liqing and Ye Yixiong to court. The chief clerk, Zhang Yimin, read the records of the original plaintiff and defendant, and Ye Zhang confirmed that they were accurate and agreed to sign them. The court had scheduled the third public trial for the 9th of this month, and the summons had already been issued. Yesterday morning, they suddenly received a telegram transferring jurisdiction, which brought the matter to a close and transferred the case to Liaoning. It is reported that on the 4th of this month, the Northeast Political Affairs Committee held a regular meeting, attended by Deputy Commander Zhang Xueliang. Seeing the reports in the newspapers about the second public trial and the slow handling of the case by the Binjiang Court, he immediately raised it for discussion. It was the consensus that the case was related to the reputation of the Northeast judicial community and the movement to reclaim extraterritoriality, so they all advocated transferring jurisdiction and returning to [歸 - incomplete sentence in original]. As for Zhang Wang Liqing, unable to collect the 7,050 yuan in drafts and unable to borrow money, and with the case further delayed, she did not know when it would end. In anxiety, her wound recurred yesterday, and her lung disease worsened. The First Goodness Hospital administered several injections, but there was still no improvement. It is also reported that after Ye is escorted to Shenyang, the Prosecutor's Office will first investigate and then summon Zhang Wang Liqing to the case. (February 7)

Implementation of Contract System in Shandong Province

▲Revising the Value of Fields and Houses

Jinan Correspondence: The Department of Finance yesterday proposed at the Provincial Government Standing Committee that all counties implement a contract system and revise the value of fields and houses, which has been approved and will be promulgated and implemented from April. The measures set by the department are as follows: "The investigation of contract tax in this province has always been a major source of income for the provincial treasury. Regulations have been promulgated and strictly enforced to the best of our ability. However, county residents are accustomed to old habits, often delaying the payment of taxes when purchasing fields and houses, or writing down the contract price, which affects tax revenue significantly. To rectify tax revenue, two measures are proposed as follows: (1) It is proposed to order all counties to implement a contract paper system as a basis for urging tax payment. The contract income depends on the number of field and house transactions. In order to investigate whether county residents have delayed paying taxes, in December of the sixth year of the Republic of China, in accordance with the contract issuance method promulgated by the Ministry, counties were ordered to establish contract issuance offices to sell contracts for use by county residents when transferring fields and houses. The county governments can use this contract stub to investigate whether there are households that have delayed paying taxes and can use it as a basis for urging tax payment. However, since its implementation, most have followed the establishment, while some have not established it due to special circumstances. If the delay is allowed to continue, it will greatly hinder the future of tax revenue. It seems that all counties should be ordered to complete the establishment of the aforementioned issuance offices, earnestly promote them, and report them. They should also prepare and equip a circulating contract sales book in accordance with the regulations, which will be circulated monthly by each issuance office for the county to check and verify, thereby urging tax payment. If any person does not purchase a contract in accordance with the regulations but pays taxes with a draft contract, the tax will not be allowed to show restriction. However, the original price of this contract was set at five copper coins per sheet for printing materials and subsidies for the office. Later, in August of the 18th year, according to the reports from Qihe Teng County and other counties that it was not enough for application, former Director Yuan changed it to ten copper coins per sheet. Recently, according to reports from various counties that the current prices of goods are expensive and still not enough for application, please increase it. After verification, it may be the case, it seems that the sales price of this item should be changed to twenty copper coins per sheet to make up for it and facilitate implementation. (2) It is proposed to order all counties to re-determine the value of fields and houses as a standard for tax collection. The original value of fields and houses was set up to prevent writing down the contract price. In the past, in the ninth and thirteenth and fourteenth years of the Republic of China, the counties were ordered three times to determine the fair price according to the actual value at that time, divided into three grades: upper, middle, and lower. If the contract price for tax payment exceeds the assessed value, the tax will still be collected according to the contract price. If it is less than the assessed value, the assessed value will be the standard. All departments have followed this in the case. However, this value varies from time to time and cannot be fixed. Currently, the value of fields and houses in various counties is more expensive than in the past. If it is not re-determined, it will not be appropriate. It seems that all counties should be ordered to re-determine and report the value of fields and houses as a standard for tax collection. The above two measures are important for rectifying the contract tax and should be carried out in order. However, the contract tax of each county, from January to the end of March of this year, has just been ordered to be collected at half the original rate of six percent for purchase and three percent for mortgage, in order to make it easy and encourage payment, and to show consideration. It should be waited until this case is over before ordering the counties to do it accordingly. The relevant details are respectfully requested for public decision." It was decided that it should be handled as proposed. (February 9)

Overflow of Ice Floes in the Yellow River in Shandong

▲Two Places Overflow in Fan County

Jinan Correspondence: The Yellow River is currently in the period of ice floe overflow, and dangerous works are emerging one after another. The people's embankment at Liao Qiao on the north bank of Fan County upstream reported two breaches with a width of eight zhang. Upon investigation, the biggest reason is that the weather this winter has been erratic, with the river ice thawing and freezing alternately. The climate in Lijin, near the sea downstream, is colder than upstream. Recently, the weather suddenly warmed, and the ice upstream thawed. Giant ice floes, several zhang in size, swept down the river like an avalanche. Seventy li from the sea, the ice had not yet thawed. The giant ice floes accumulated and could not move down, causing the river water to rise. Zhang Lianjia, the director of the River Affairs Bureau, personally inspected the downstream on the 5th and returned to the bureau on the 7th. On the 7th, 8th, and 9th, the weather suddenly turned cold again, and the river ice re-froze to above Luokou, while there were still unfrozen areas in Luokou and Qinghezhen below, where the ice floes accumulated and could not move down, causing the river water to rise another eight chi. The dikes on both sides of the river were only one chi above the water. The dangerous works at Wangzaojia and Jizi stayed downstream, racing against the clock to prevent the danger, but the ground was frozen like stone, making it impossible to obtain earth. The weather was cold, and the water was cold, and the ice floes were too large. Those who were rushing to the rescue could not get into the water and dared not get close. According to the old regulations of the Qing Dynasty, river affairs personnel could be exempted from punishment for ice floe overflow in the Yellow River, and it is for this reason. The dangerous situation this time is unprecedented. Director Zhang Lianjia went downstream again yesterday to supervise the rescue efforts. The emergency telegrams from various places are recorded as follows: (1) To Zhang Jun, Director of the Jinan River Affairs Bureau: It is hoped that you will understand the song telegram. According to Xu Desheng, the head of the first section in the north, the Jiang Fan chief reported that the river water has risen one chi since winter, a total of five chi. New small embankments are still leaking. The engineering section chief of the Liao Work Committee, Zhang Shi, is on-site to take charge of everything. He immediately supervises the Fan chief to lead soldiers and civilians to rush to protect and block with straw. Unexpectedly, a leak occurred not far from the material factory to the west of the West Dam. The water was turbulent. Because the ground was frozen like stone, it was impossible to obtain soil. At noon on the winter day, it overflowed more than eight zhang. When Jiang Fan chief met with Zhang Gu, he first set up a method to rescue and protect. According to the urgent telegram from Wei Shen, the river water fell three chi from Dong Hai to Jiang You. In the afternoon of that day, Wang, the magistrate of Fan County, brought Zhong Lian chief and others to Liao to meet with Zhang Gu to discuss the work on the Zizhi day. First block the west mouth, then block the east mouth. In addition to ordering Liu Fan chief Jiuxing to assist, he will also clamp the river from Jiang Mao to Zhishi, and the water rose four chi and two cun. I only stopped knowing this morning, etc. Based on this, in addition to the urgent telegram to Zhong Lian chief Xu sub-section chief and others to speed up the method of blocking the mouth and report the preparation situation at any time, Li He Dian Chen, please ask for your appraisal, Chief Chen Wenmo, knocking You. (2) Chen Wenmo, Chief of the Shilibu Upstream Section: I know the Yuyou telegram. According to the report, the Liao West Dam overflowed more than eight zhang to the west, and new small embankments leaked. Wang, the magistrate of Fan County, took Zhong Lian chief to Liao and agreed with Zhang Gu that Zizhi day will start work, first blocking the west mouth and then blocking the east mouth. Based on this, it is appropriate to rush to prepare for blocking the Liao Work Ling Fan overflow. However, in the cold weather, hasty blocking may not be stable. You, the chief of the general section, went to work in person on the day to handle it appropriately, and report the engineering situation at any time as necessary. Director Zhang Lianjia Gengyin. (9th)

Records of Bandit Suppression in Henan Province

▲ Sixth Division Vigorously Attacks Long-Time Ferocious Bandits

▲ More Than Two Thousand Hostages Rescued

A dispatch from Xuchang reports that Zhao Guantao, Commander of the Sixth Division, concurrently serving as Director of the Third Pacification Zone of Henan, immediately dispatched his troops to various locations for garrison duty based on the severity of the bandit situation, and had already completed the deployments. Unexpectedly, Zhang Tietou, a bandit leader who had long entrenched himself in Taikang, led several thousand men, fully equipped with firearms and ammunition, intending to operate within the pacification area of the Sixth Division, kidnapping people for ransom everywhere, tearing up tickets, and setting fires. Any villages they passed through were completely looted. On the 28th of last month, they suddenly intruded into the northern border of Xuchang. Upon hearing the news, the people of the entire county were terrified. Zhao Guantao, the director of the pacification zone, believed that this band of bandits could not be spared a severe suppression. He immediately ordered the independent brigade under his command, led by Wang Yunshan, to dispatch a regiment under Si Yugui to intercept them, using a rescued hostage as a guide. They encountered the bandits northwest of Chenlou in Xiaogongzhai and immediately opened fire. The bandits, numbering several thousand, resisted stubbornly, leading to a fierce battle lasting seven hours. Over four hundred bandits were killed and twenty-four were captured alive. The bandit forces were unable to withstand the assault and fled in disarray to the northwest. On the spot, over one hundred and thirty mules, horses, cattle, and donkeys, more than fifty miscellaneous rifles, over thirty fake flags, and more than two thousand hostages were seized. The regiment, while ordering the troops to pursue and track down the fleeing bandits, also escorted the captured prisoners, mules, horses, cattle, and donkeys to the Xuchang Pacification Headquarters. Commander Zhao then instructed personnel from the division to work with the Xuchang County Government Public Security Bureau to investigate the hometowns and circumstances of the kidnapped hostages and to make proper arrangements for their overnight stay. The next day, they were given dry rations and travel expenses and sent back to their respective hometowns. The total number included 414 from Luyi, 401 from Chenzhou, 352 from Yanling, 304 from Xihua, 169 from Fugou, 92 from Linying, 8 from Xuchang, 4 from Qi County, and 3 from Xiangcheng. Various public groups and organizations in Xuchang, recognizing that Commander Zhao's arrival in Xuchang and swift action to suppress the long-standing bandits marked a significant achievement, specially entrusted Zheng Kanghou, the magistrate of Xuchang County, to host a banquet in celebration. Magistrate Zheng, acting as chairman, rose to give a speech during the banquet, stating that after the esteemed division assumed command of the Third Pacification Zone of Henan, it immediately dispersed a large band of bandits and rescued over two thousand hostages, setting a new record since the suppression of bandits in Henan began. Furthermore, the soldiers of the esteemed division were disciplined and caused no alarm wherever they went, serving as a model for the military. He, as the magistrate, represented the people of the county in offering a toast to express their gratitude. Commander Zhao then rose to respond, stating that since he began leading troops, he had always advocated the principle of "strict suppression of bandits and absolute non-disturbance of the people." However, he emphasized that to completely eradicate local bandits, the political sector must organize rural reforms, and the people must promptly report any suspicious activities. Since he had assumed the position of Director of the Pacification Zone, he would do everything in his power to protect the people of the region and ensure their safety and security.

Battalion Commander Zhang and Inspector Yang led the soldiers and bravely advanced, but they were outnumbered and almost surrounded by the bandits. After several hours, the bandits began to flee. In the beginning of their marriage, they were still harmonious. Last summer, they suddenly had disagreements. However, Zhu's parents also said that their daughter-in-law did not manage the household properly and was dissatisfied with many things. Shen Guanjin Gruesomely Murdered: Shen Guanjin, a business owner in Erzao Hong, a county district, was previously kidnapped by bandits and a ransom of 100,000 was demanded. Months have passed with no news. The other day, a male corpse buried alive was found next to a grave of a certain family on Qujia Road outside the East Gate. After an examination by the county coroner, the corpse was placed in a coffin, sealed, and put up for identification. At that time, rumors spread that the corpse was Shen Guanjin, murdered by bandits. His family, upon hearing the news, inquired about everything from the coroner, believed that the corpse's appearance and clothing were similar to Guanjin's, and claimed it from the county. It was confirmed to be Guanjin's body. The family members carried the body back, changed the coffin, and held a funeral. They also requested the county government to strictly apprehend the bandits involved in this case and bring them to justice.

Wuxi

Postponement of the Implementation of the New Pawnshop Regulations: The pawnshop associations in various counties of Jiangsu Province have repeatedly appealed to the provincial government regarding the case of overdue redemption fees after the New Year, but have not received approval. Most of the capital of pawnshops throughout the province is less than 100,000 yuan, and the actual interest charged is often less than six months. Although the nominal monthly interest rate is two percent, after deducting occupancy, unsalable goods, and all expenses, the net profit is only between five and six percent. With increasing expenses, further reductions in revenue would make it impossible to maintain operations. Therefore, on the 5th of this month, representatives of pawnshop associations from various counties went to the provincial capital to submit a petition, which was accepted by the provincial authorities. They were allowed to postpone the implementation and were scheduled to hold a meeting of pawnshop associations from the entire province in Suzhou on January 15th to provide further encouragement. However, the county government had already received an order from the Construction Department to instruct pawnshops to implement the new regulations and had issued a public notice. Yesterday, the County Chamber of Commerce, considering that the current time is during the winter season and the end of the year, when pawnshops should be redeeming more and pawning less, stated that overdue redemption fees are currently of little consequence. Based on the provincial government's approval to postpone the implementation, the Chamber of Commerce sent a letter to the county government requesting that it not urge pawnshops too much until the provincial pawnshop association has held its meeting in order to maintain the pawnshop business.

The Outcome of the Prostitution Case Involving a Police Officer: Zhou Runshi, an investigator from the Civil Affairs Department's police affairs department, was accused by Shen Xiang of soliciting prostitution and abducting his concubine Zhou Xingzhen. After the county government transferred the relevant witnesses in the case to the county court, Zhou Runshi, who was in custody, hired lawyer Zhou Shuijin to submit a petition to the court, arguing that soliciting prostitution does not constitute a criminal offense but only involves personal morality and should only be subject to administrative punishment. He further argued that there was no suspicion of abduction and requested an impartial investigation and acquittal. After receiving the petition, the county court summoned the plaintiff Shen Xiang, his mother Ms. Yu, his wife Ms. Yu, En Rui, a member of the third branch of the Public Security Bureau, and the defendants in custody, Zhou Runshi, Zhou Xingzhen, Wang Lihong, and Wang Chongxi, for questioning by prosecutor Zhu Zonghai. After a lengthy investigation, prosecutor Zhu announced in court that the abduction part of the case would not be prosecuted, and the prostitution part was a violation of police regulations and would be transferred to the Public Security Bureau for sentencing. The plaintiffs Shen Xiang and Ms. Yu were dismissed. Zhou Runshi, Zhou Xingzhen, Wang Lihong, and Wang Chongxi were temporarily returned to custody to await punishment by the Public Security Bureau. Qin Enrui was released on bail. After the verdict, the plaintiff Shen Xiang declared in court that he was dissatisfied and argued vehemently. The defendant Zhou Runshi also stated in court that since the plaintiff's accusations had been dismissed, the plaintiff should be punished for false accusation and defamation. Prosecutor Zhu ordered a separate lawsuit to be filed. Thus, the scandalous case of a police officer soliciting prostitution came to an end.

Temporary Suspension of Self-Organized Feast Donation Collection: The County Party and Government Consolidation Committee, based on a letter from the third district branch transferring a request to the county government to abolish the education donation for self-organized feasts for weddings and funerals, immediately forwarded the letter to the county government. They engaged in secret affairs more than once, and their love was as deep as that of a married couple. Recently, Chen Afu suffered from inguinal hernia typhus, and his illness was severe and unresponsive to medication. He died the other day. Upon hearing the news, his lover Xi Mei was heartbroken. She went to the Chen family to attend the funeral and immediately developed a sense of world-weariness. Yesterday, she walked to the nearby river and committed suicide by drowning. She was later pulled out of the water, but she had already passed away.

The report stated that Jiangyin is situated with its northern boundary adjacent to the Yangtze River, with Xia Gang to the west extending directly north to the river, and with the area from Lupu Port directly north to the Jianghuang Earth and Stone Village area, and with the area from the Peach Blossom Port extending directly north to the Jiang Port. The bays and ports are complex and easy for bandits to use for concealment. Therefore, in areas such as Huangtu Earth and Stone Village, Jiajiatou, and the east and west Zhuang areas, bandit leaders such as Gao Xiaosheng and Yang Yaoda were causing disturbances. Bandit leader Yu Abing was executed, and bandit leaders Zhu Awu, Shen Awen, Xia Peizhi, and Liu Hongxi were captured. The remaining bandits fled north across the Yangtze River, and the bandit situation was slightly reduced. In the northeast, there are mountains and ports such as Changshan, Xiangshan, Zhangqi Mountain, Panlong Mountain, Huangshan Port, Baisha Port, Wushan Port, Zhangjia Port, Hucao Port, and Duan Shan Port, which are intertwined and also easy for bandits to hide in. Bandit leaders Chen Weiwu, Fan Jinquan, and Chen Latong have been sentenced. Bandit Wang Ziming killed himself, and bandit Tao Jigen and Tang Awen were shot dead. Bandit Liu Ziwen and Wang Shaowen were captured. The remaining bandits also fled successively across the Yangtze River, and the bandit situation was also slightly reduced. The southern part of the county is inland, and there are fewer bandits. After the execution of bandit Zhou A Kui, the situation in the western townships has also become slightly more stable. This is the general situation.

Gaoyou

Summary of the Fourth District Affairs Meeting: Cheng, the chief of the Sixth District of the Gaoyou Maritime Provincial Public Team, convened the fourth district affairs meeting with subordinates in the district at 3 pm yesterday. It was resolved to report to the People's Department for nuclear indication, and to order the head police to ensure that the wheel fare subsidies are appropriate. (2) The restructuring plan of this district has been instructed by the Qinmin Office, and is feasible in theory, but how will it be carried out in the future? It was resolved that husband candidates should be those who are loyal to their duties as the standard and that the discharged personnel should be submitted to the People's Department by this district for prior recruitment. The issue of unpaid salaries shall be addressed first. (3) Regarding the order to report bandit affairs on a weekly basis, it was resolved that this district shall draft a form to be issued to all subordinate teams, to be filled out and reported on a weekly basis.

Anhui Bandits Have Been Suppressed: Jiang Guochang (also known as Three-Legged), a notorious bandit in Anhui Province, recently led three to four hundred bandits to besiege Dachang Gangcheng Town. However, due to the arrival of reinforcements, the bandits fled into Gaoyou territory. The county government ordered Shi, the captain of the police battalion, to lead his team to suppress them and telegraphed the Pacification Supervisory Office to send troops to block them. It is now reported that the bandits have been suppressed by Liang Guanying's subordinates in conjunction with the Anhui army. The twelfth district of this county is now safe as usual.

Nantong

Provincial Committee to Handle Land Classification: The provincial government, recognizing that many new and old cases of unclassified sandy and wasteland existed in Nantong, appointed Jiang Yongyi to Nantong to work with the county government's finance bureau to handle the matter. Commissioner Jiang began to investigate on the 10th, following the Changshu precedent, first ordering each household to pay supplementary grain at a rate of two to four yuan per mu.

Pingchao District Chief Suspended Due to Bandit Case: Zhang Kui, the Pingchao district chief, has been suspended because he was involved in the Wu Yang bandit case in his jurisdiction. He is currently being investigated and interrogated by the military law commission. He has been granted bail pending investigation and confirmation.

Deadline to Reorganize County Security Corps: The county government received an order from the province urging the entire county security corps to be reorganized according to the draft system as soon as possible. Starting from March 1st, commissioners will be appointed to inspect and brand firearms.

Pinghu

Kidnapping and Robbery Cases Near Mao Kou: More than forty bandits swarmed to Zhang Zhangbei, Zhang Zhangjia, and Zhang Lin's house in Huangdu, about three miles from Xindi in Pinghu North Township, the other night (8th). The men woke up from their dreams and quickly hid on the roof with their own rifles. The bandits broke down the door and looted all the valuables. Three women were kidnapped. When the bandits were about to leave, Zhang Lin fired several shots from the roof, killing one bandit. Big Soil Dealer Sentenced to a Fine: Big soil dealer Zhang Zhangbei from Pinghu Xianghong Lane, was caught by the patrol team during the term of Shen County Head and transferred to the county. Because Zhang Lin was on the run, his wife Xingbao reported to the police, where she was detained pending resolution. After Wu County Head took office, he cleared the backlog of cases and sentenced her to three months imprisonment on the 10th and a fine of four hundred yuan. After Mr. Li paid two hundred silver dollars, he requested that she be released on bail, which was granted.

Huzhou

Huzhou-Changxing Bus Robbed by Bandits: The bus from Huzhou to Changxing on the Hangzhou-Changxing highway was robbed by four bandits at 12:30 noon on the 6th. Near Yangjiapu, near Santianmen, four bandits suddenly appeared, each with a handgun. The bus was stopped and the bandits guarded the doors, forcing the passengers to get off the bus one by one and searching them all. Jin Da Jiang and his colleagues were said to have suffered the greatest losses among the passengers. Since the opening of the Hangzhou-Changxing road, there have been several cases of bandits robbing the road, so passengers are quite dissatisfied.

Lu Caisheng's Home in Southern Township Robbed by Bandits: Lu Caisheng, who is over sixty years old and lives in Lukiawan, near the border between Linghu and Qingshan in the southern township of this city, had a small well-off family. At 5 pm the other day, a dozen bandits with foreign accents and armed with firearms suddenly broke into his home, overturning boxes and containers. They looted all the clothing, silver dollars, and other items. Before leaving, they kidnapped Caisheng's daughter-in-law and granddaughter-in-law. Fortunately, Caisheng was out on business, so he was spared the shock.

Hangzhou

Dispatch of Elite Troops to Suppress Gang Bandits: The Zhejiang Provincial Government, believing that Gang bandits in eastern Jiangxi were rampant, decided to consolidate security and, in addition to sending security training teams to block the border, also submitted a request to the general headquarters to send Tang Brigade of the Fourth Division to Jiangxi to defeat the bandit groups. The training team was also withdrawn to Jiang to be stationed permanently. Now, the Gang bandits have revived and continue to cause disturbances. In addition to ordering the training team to strictly defend and suppress the bandits, Xu Tingyao, the commander of the Fourth Division stationed in the province, recently sent four more battalions of infantry, towed by the Jianggan Taihua Zhenxing and Shuijiang Company's ships, to the border between Zhejiang and Jiangxi to suppress the bandits with the aim of annihilating them in one fell swoop.

Abolition of Lunar New Year and Prohibition of Work Stoppages: The Hangzhou Municipal Government issued a public notice yesterday to prohibit workers from stopping work for the abolished Lunar New Year. The notice stated that the Standing Committee of the Central Executive Committee had passed measures to promote the National Calendar, and an extract of the notice had been issued in August of the tenth year. The first item stated that the Lunar New Year holiday would be moved to the National Calendar New Year. Therefore, there is no provision for holidays during the abolished Lunar New Year. As the abolished Lunar New Year is approaching, there is a deep concern that factory workers will continue to ask for leave for the year in accordance with old customs. It is reiterated and warned that at the beginning of this reform, all workers must understand this and jointly promote innovation. It is highly anticipated.

Ningbo

Bandits Kill Gate Sentry and Confiscate Firearms: Last year, the county government stationed a team of security guards, totaling twelve men, at the Chang Temple in Songlin Paixi, Fenghua, because of the rampant bandits in the area. The team leader, Huang, had ten rifles and a six-inch handgun. At 2 pm yesterday, fifty bandits suddenly arrived from Tonggong Ridge and approached the temple. They opened fire at the temple gate with wooden-cased guns, killing one gate sentry. Another gate sentry was captured by the bandits, who then rushed in. Team Leader Huang knew things were bad and jumped over the wall to avoid them. Nine rifles and a six-inch handgun were confiscated. Fortunately, none of the other team members were injured. The temple was completely burned down by the bandits, and one gate sentry was kidnapped. After the incident, the Fenghua County Government sent police to pursue the bandits, but they had already gone far away. Several leaflets were found near Lingchang Temple, instructing the people of Paixi to pay 10,000 yuan in foreign currency and to contact them at Tonggong Ridge within a specified period of time.

Stock Exchange to be Established Soon: Twenty-five major merchants from Shanghai and Ningbo, including Wei Bozhen and Chen Nanqin, have launched a stock exchange in Ningbo. It is learned that these founders have each advanced 8,000 yuan in share capital, totaling about 200,000 yuan. They are currently looking for a suitable location and will open soon.

Local News

City Police Chief Chen Xizeng Assumes Office Yesterday

▲ Summons all Staff for Instructions

▲ Separate Swearing-in Ceremony to be Scheduled

Mr. Chen Xizeng, the newly appointed Director of the Shanghai Municipal Police Bureau, assumed his duties at the bureau yesterday morning at 10:00 a.m. upon the order of the Municipal Government, in view of the urgent winter defense period and local security. A separate swearing-in ceremony will be held at a later date, inviting guests from all sectors to observe. A summary of yesterday's handover proceedings is detailed below:

▲ Handover Proceedings: Director Chen, accompanied by Chief Inspector Wang Yufen, arrived at the bureau at 10:00 a.m. yesterday morning. Prior to their arrival, the Police Brigade and all staff of the Public Security Bureau, along with the military band, were assembled in the bureau's courtyard, playing music to welcome them. The new director was led to the director's office by Section Chief Huang Guangdou and others, where he received the seal of the Shanghai Municipal Police Bureau and the handover inventory. After a brief deployment, he summoned all staff for instructions. Those who came to the Public Security Bureau yesterday morning to congratulate Mr. Chen included Secretary-General Yu Hongjun, representing the Municipal Government, as well as Yu Qiaqing, Wang Xiaolai, Ye Huijun, Wen Lanting, Tang Naikang, Xu Peihuang, Zhu Zhongzhou, Tan Shaoliang, and many others.

▲ Director's Address: "Brothers, I am a revolutionary soldier. I am honored to be appointed to take charge of public security in this city and to meet all of you. Many of the officers, both senior and junior, within and outside the bureau, are former colleagues and comrades who have shared hardships. Some are classmates and old friends, and some are new comrades whom I have not yet met. However, since we are all serving in the same organization, it is important that each person be loyal to their duty. Whether we knew each other before or not is irrelevant. There should be no distinctions or boundaries. The government selects people based on talent. I will treat everyone, regardless of whether they are new or old comrades, whether I know them or not, based on their job responsibilities, assessing their performance, and judging their merits. The duty of public security personnel is like the red blood cells in the human body, constantly working every moment to ensure public safety. You must have a spirit of sacrifice, sacrificing personal happiness and tranquility to preserve public safety, so that you can be worthy of the Party, the country, and society, and be considered to have fulfilled your duties. In officialdom, it is common for subordinates to be anxious and even seek connections to secure their positions whenever a superior changes. I believe that if you want to know your own status, you should only ask yourself whether you have fulfilled your responsibilities and whether your performance is good. If your performance is good, even if no one speaks for you, I will trust you greatly. If your performance is poor or non-existent, even thousands of recommendations from wealthy people will not be tolerated. I do not care whether you have a personal relationship with me, or whether we have shared hardships, and I do not distinguish between those appointed by the previous director and those appointed by the current director. I serve the Party and the country, and I only recognize the Party and the country. I do not recognize the faces of wealthy people. Personal relationships are personal, and I will never allow them to interfere with public duties. I hope everyone will recognize their responsibilities, work together, and put aside all personal gains and losses, as well as old habits, in order to be worthy of the Party, the country, and society. Then you will be my good friends and loyal comrades. Governing does not require many words, but relies entirely on action. I will use my own eyes to see your merits and demerits in practice. No matter how nice someone speaks, I will never rely on hearsay. We are currently in the winter defense period, and the responsibility of public security is even more important than usual. Maintaining social security is our sole duty, and fulfilling our responsibilities is an opportunity for everyone to be assessed. As for all superficial formalities, I will not speak of them, nor is it necessary to speak of them. I hope to work with everyone to invigorate our spirits and work together."

▲ Inauguration Notice: Notice is hereby given that, pursuant to Order No. 624 of the Municipal Government, Chen Xizeng is hereby appointed as the Director of the Shanghai Municipal Police Bureau. In addition to submitting a request to the Executive Yuan for referral to the National Government for appointment, you are hereby directed to proceed to the bureau to assume your duties immediately, in order to emphasize public service, and to report the date of your assumption of office. This order, etc. In compliance with this, the Director of this Bureau assumed his duties on February 11th. In addition to submitting separate reports and orders, this notice is hereby issued for the information of all citizens of this city. This notice.

▲ Chen's Brief Biography: Native of Wuxing, Zhejiang. Graduate of the Zhejiang Army Military Academy. Served as Special Officer at the Whampoa Military Academy in Guangdong, Staff Officer of the Eastern Expeditionary Army Headquarters of the National Revolutionary Army, Secretary of the Headquarters of the Commander-in-Chief of the National Revolutionary Army, Director of the Rear Guard Office of the General Political Department of the National Revolutionary Army, Director of the Guangdong Telecommunications Administration, Supervisory Committee Member of the Shanghai Municipal Party Headquarters, Reorganization Committee Member of the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company, and Director of the Shanghai Telegraph Bureau.

▲ Staff Appointments: Mr. Chen made no changes to the existing staff, except for the resignation of Xu Jiahan, Head of the First Section, which was announced yesterday. Miao Zhexian was appointed as Head of the First Section. Feng Yuanxiang, Ji Qianqiu, and Jian Qiujian were appointed as Secretaries. Hong Qi was appointed as Secretary and Director of the Foreign Affairs Division.

▲ Guangdong Army to Withdraw from Guangxi in Two Stages

▲ Post-Situation Period Temporarily Set at Three Months

Ma Xiaojun, Counselor of the General Headquarters, has been instrumental in mediating for a peaceful resolution in Guangxi. The Eighth Route Army of Guangdong entering Guangxi will withdraw from Guangxi in two stages. Huang Shaoxiong, Wu Tingyang, and Chen Shisan will stay in Shanghai for a maximum of one week and then take a boat to Hong Kong and return to Guangxi. It has not yet been decided whether I will go with them. I generally plan to stay in Nanjing to handle everything, etc.

Dredging of the Wusong River Commences Yesterday

▲ Shanghai River Bureau Receives Commission Letter from Mayor Zhang

The Shanghai Times reported that the proposal to dredge the Suzhou River has been advocated for twelve years. Due to various reasons, it has not been implemented for a long time. Until today, the Shanghai River Bureau has been commissioned by the Special Committee for Dredging this River to start construction. It is scheduled to be completed in six years from the mouth of the Suzhou River to Yujidun. The bureau received a commission letter from Mayor Zhang on Monday and will begin work today (11th). A reporter met with the Chief Engineer of the Shanghai River Bureau yesterday, who stated that the scope of the dredging project is currently limited to the Shanghai city boundary, starting from Yujidun, approximately five miles west of the Bund, to the mouth of the Suzhou River. It is planned to start construction near the mouth of the river. Two dredgers have been dispatched, one at the mouth of the Outer White Bridge and one between the Outer White Bridge and Zhaofeng Road, to dredge in sections. The dredged mud will be transported to the bureau's mud pumping station downstream of the Huangpu River to fill shallows. In addition, small crab claw-style dredgers will need to be added to dredge the upper reaches. They are currently being built at the Jiangnan Shipyard and are expected to be completed and put into use around this autumn. The dredging depth is planned to be six feet deep even at the lowest water level, so as not to affect the safety of the river bank. However, this project is quite large. According to the current plan, it will take six years to complete.

Guangji Returned to Shanghai Yesterday

▲ Account of Pirate Discovery on Board

▲ Chao Wu Warship Dispatches Team to Escort

▲ Travelers Can Be Assured of Safety in the Future

The China Merchants Steam Navigation Company's Guangji ship discovered weapons and pirates on board, thereby averting a robbery. This matter has been reported in this newspaper. Yesterday, the ship returned to Shanghai from Wenzhou. A passenger named Mr. Li, who is familiar with the reporter, recounted the truth of the Guangji ship's discovery of pirates, which is worthy of publication. The details are as follows:

▲ Bandits Mix into Ship: When the Guangji ship left Wenzhou on the morning of the 6th, the bandits had already disguised themselves as passengers and mixed into the cabins. The bandit leader was very young, only 26 years old. He arrived on the ship in advance and booked cabin No. 9. He was wearing a camel绒 robe and carrying a leather bag. When the ship set sail, the crew did not pay attention. After the anchor was raised, the bandit leader, under the alias of Hu Acun, went to and from various cabins, carefully inspecting the luggage of the passengers, seemingly assessing their wealth. A passenger saw that his eyes were shining brightly and he was walking back and forth suspiciously. A passenger secretly reported to the captain and asked him to pay attention to this person's movements. Sure enough, he was seen signaling to passengers in the steerage. The captain determined that he was undoubtedly a bandit and reported it to the police for arrest, and the case was solved.

▲ Marine Police Search and Seize Weapons: The captain remained calm and sailed to Huanghuaguan outside the port of Wenzhou and dropped anchor. The Chao Wu warship of the Marine Police Department was berthed there. The captain reported to the captain of the warship and asked him to send police to search. The Chao Wu warship immediately sent ten armed marine police officers to board the ship. First, they searched Hu Acun in cabin No. 9. At first, the bandit leader refused to allow the leather bag to be searched. The marine police then used a bayonet to pry open the leather bag, revealing twelve brand-new Browning pistols. The marine police officers immediately subdued the bandit Hu. The bandit wanted to take out a gun to open fire, but it was too late. A pistol was also found on the bandit's body. He was immediately escorted to the warship, and police officers were sent to guard the cabin entrances, preventing anyone from escaping, as further searches were required.

▲ Twelve More Bandits Apprehended: After the bandit leader arrived on the warship, he was interrogated by the captain and confessed that there were a total of twenty accomplices who boarded the ship to rob. The marine police boarded the Guangji ship for a second time and searched the steerage cabin one by one. Fifteen suspicious persons were found and escorted to the warship for further interrogation. Among them, twelve were identified by the bandit leader as accomplices. Three people proved that they were passengers. The captain detained the bandits and released the passengers back to the ship.

▲ Confession of Pirate Organization: Hu Acun was the leader of the bandits. Two or three other leaders were also arrested. Interrogated by the captain, they confessed that there were four more bandits on the ship, but they could not be identified, or they may not have boarded the ship. They also claimed that this robbery was carefully planned. More than 100 accomplices and six bandit ships had been dispatched 100 miles away from Huanghuaguan in Wenzhou waters, preparing to take action on the ship tonight and unload the stolen goods there. They also confessed that they planned to rob not only the Guangji ship, but also other ships going to Shanghai, Taiwan, and Wenzhou one by one. They hoped to rob 300,000 yuan from the Guangji ship.

▲ Raid on Bandit Nest in Wenzhou: On the morning of the 7th, the marine police escorted the third bandit leader back to Wenzhou from the Guangji ship. The security team boarded the ship at the port again for a search, but found no trace of the four bandits, knowing that they had not yet boarded the ship. They then took the bandit to the bandit's nest mentioned by him, in a folk house in Dongmen. The security team went to search, but the four bandits had escaped. Only an old woman was found, and a wooden shell gun was found. They were immediately taken to the Fourth Command of the Wenzhou Security Command for interrogation. The bandit was then escorted to the Chao Wu warship for joint handling.

▲ Guangji Protected to Shanghai: The Guangji sailed from Wenzhou to Shanghai via Huanghuaguan on the 8th, but dared not sail because there were more than 100 pirates waiting on the sea. The Chao Wu warship was requested to send troops to escort them. The captain selected seven capable police officers with machine guns and rifles to board the ship to escort them to Shanghai. They arrived in Shanghai safely yesterday. All the passengers and their families were deeply grateful to the organizers of the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company for their effective handling. The passengers went to the bureau to express their gratitude after arriving in Shanghai. The ship will resume its voyage to Wenzhou today.

Report of the Canadian Trade Mission After Returning Home

▲ Submitted to the Canadian Government by the Canadian Chamber of Commerce

When the Canadian Trade Mission visited Shanghai last year, Chinese groups and individuals expressed their sincere hope that the harsh restrictions on the entry of Orientals would be lifted and the treatment of overseas Chinese would be improved. According to news from Ottawa, after the mission returned to Canada, it proposed in its report to the Canadian government that the government study whether the regulations governing the entry of merchants and tourists from the Far East could be amended in order to enhance friendship between Canada and the Japanese and Chinese nations and facilitate the development of commerce. In addition, (1) it requested the government to increase the number of trade commissioners stationed in the Far East, especially in northern China, where there is currently no special commissioner; (2) the cost of telegraphs between the Far East and Canada is too high, which hinders commerce, and the government is requested to study the possibility of establishing wireless telephones to reduce merchants' costs; (3) it requested the Department of Commerce and the Department of Finance to investigate the separation of goods indirectly shipped from the Far East to Canada and to find ways to encourage direct trade in order to reduce the rise and fall of trade between Japan and China and Canada. The above four points are all more related to the Far East. It is reported that this report was formally submitted to the Canadian government by the Canadian Chamber of Commerce on January 22nd.

▲ Talk After Yu Qiaqing Returned to Shanghai

Silk Industry Business Tax Approved for Reduction

▲ Telegram Report from Silk Relief Association

The China National Silk Relief Association sent a telegram yesterday announcing the success of reducing the business tax on the silk industry: It is known to all silk industry groups in various provinces and cities that when various provinces are implementing business taxes, the Zhejiang Provincial Department of Finance first proposed a tax rate of 30 per mille for the silk industry. Later, during the meeting, the representatives of the silk industry strongly argued for a reduction to 15 per mille. This exceeded the highest rate of 2 per mille for business tax collection in various provinces promulgated by the Executive Yuan by nearly eight times. Not only is it difficult for businesses to bear, but it also regards silk as a luxury item that should be banned. This is contrary to the Central Government's intention to promote domestic silk weaving. If this is not contested, it is feared that various provinces will follow suit, and the future of the silk industry will decline and eventually disappear. Hundreds of thousands of farmers and silkworms in Jiangsu and Zhejiang will lose their source of livelihood, and the clothing materials of our country's 400 million compatriots will rely entirely on imported goods. The relationship is so great that we cannot bear to say it all. As expected, the tax rate in Jiangsu Province is also the same as that of Zhejiang Province at 15 per mille, while Fujian Province even follows the initial draft of Zhejiang Province, stipulating it as 30 per mille. Even compared to the lowest tax rate in Hubei Province, it is still 5 per mille. Therefore, the silk industry in Jiangsu, Zhejiang, and Shanghai, for the sake of the survival of the domestic silk industry, was forced to push forward and publicly elected representatives to go to the central government and various ministries and courtyards to petition. Yan Song followed Luo Qinghua, Zhu Mouxian, Zheng Bing, Pan Xiangsheng, Jiang Linshu, Shen Zicha, Wu Xingcha, Lou Fengshao, Cai Liangyou, Lin Zhaorong, and other representatives, rushing to Nanjing and Beijing to explain to the authorities the reasons why the silk industry must reduce taxes. Fortunately, the authorities adopted them and promised to consider them. Today, we respectfully read the Executive Yuan's notice that the request of the silk industry that the business tax rate collected by various provinces should not exceed 2 per mille to protect it is in line with the Central Government's previous approval of the relief of the silk weaving industry and should be approved. We deeply appreciate the Executive Yuan's virtue of maintaining domestic production and caring for farmers and merchants. We are deeply grateful and share the same feelings. Therefore, we specially send a telegram to inform you and hope that you will note it. If the business tax rate on the silk industry in various provincial and municipal governments still exceeds 2 per mille, you should request corrections at any time to emphasize government orders. The reason why this tax reduction was achieved is due to the Central Government's willingness to accept public opinion and benefit silk merchants, and the representatives of the silk industry in Jiangsu, Zhejiang, and Shanghai did not hesitate to travel and appeal, and the Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce and the Secretary of the Compilation Committee, Mr. Yan Esheng, took the lead in drafting and publicizing as much as possible, so that the feelings of the people could be conveyed and the government authorities could be moved. We hereby inform you of this and commend the hard work. Chairman Yan Song of the China National Silk Relief Association kowtows.

Ministry of Industry Permits Exemption of Tobacco Industry Inspection Fees

The Ministry of Industry yesterday approved the Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce's request to the Nanyang Huacheng and Eryan factories to transport tobacco leaves to Shandong, where the Qingdao Inspection Bureau collected inspection fees. The electric request for review and approval and the order to exempt fees to maintain the tobacco industry, etc., were approved, saying: "The electric message has been received. Commodity inspection is related to improving commodity reputation and supervising production improvement. It is of utmost importance and a responsibility of the Ministry, which is difficult to stop. For the sake of both inspection administration and commercial hardship, the Qingdao Commodity Inspection Bureau has been ordered, except for thoroughly inspected cotton and commodities specially approved by the Ministry, to exempt all non-export commodities from inspection fees to show consideration. You should be informed immediately and also inform others accordingly."

Electric Request to Revise the Business Tax Rate in Jiangsu Province

▲ National Federation of Chambers of Commerce Sends Electric Message to the National Government to Order the Provincial Government to Reconsider

The National Federation of Chambers of Commerce sent a public telegram to the National Government's Ministry of Finance and Ministry of Industry yesterday, stating: "Recently, the Jiangsu Yixing County Chamber of Commerce's electric message stated that the business tax rate implemented in Jiangsu Province exceeds the key points set by the Ministry by a large amount. After the Zhejiang business tax rate was revealed in the newspapers, various industries in Shanghai have been appealing for a reduction in the tax rate. Now, the Jiangsu tax rate is even higher than the Zhejiang tax rate. Furthermore, the match industry has already collected a unified tax and is included in the business tax. Tobacco and alcohol have license fees, but the business tax rate is included in the brewing industry. Domestic silk and satin are forcibly listed as luxury goods and charged the highest tax rate. All these repeated and harsh details not only overwhelm the businesses but also greatly affect the livelihoods of ordinary people. Arbitrary taxation is a great loss to the country's original intention to resolutely abolish tariffs. If various provinces follow suit, the key points set by the Ministry will become mere formalities, and the suffering of the businesses will be extreme. We hereby send this electric message to your association, hoping that you will jointly fight for this. We pray that you will promptly order the Jiangsu Provincial Government to seriously review and properly revise it, so that consideration can still be given to the people amidst the resistance. President Bei Kanghou of the National Federation of Chambers of Commerce respectfully kowtows."

Request to Exempt or Reduce Business Tax

▲ Qian Shops: The Municipal Committee for the Study of Business Tax Regulations telegraphed the Ministry of Finance yesterday, requesting exemption of the business tax on Qian shops, stating: "Article 1 of the supplementary measures for the outline of business tax collection in various provinces stipulates that banks may be exempted from business tax in accordance with special companies. However, Qian shops, which also bear the responsibility of regulating social finance and do not use commodities as the object, are uniquely lacking in this. According to the principles of things, it seems to be unequal. We dare to submit an electric request to the Ministry, praying that the Ministry will approve the exemption of the business tax on Qian shops, which have a long history and similar business nature, in accordance with the tax exemption precedent for banks, in order to show support and conform to equality, for the sake of public convenience."

▲ Candle Industry: The Candle Industry Association sent a letter to the Municipal Chamber of Commerce yesterday, requesting that the Ministry of Finance forward it to the Jiangsu and Zhejiang provincial governments for correction. The reason is that the output of the candle industry can rise in time, resist foreign goods, save profits, and help the lower classes and promote the strength of the people. The government should not have time to reward and promote it, so how can it increase the tax rate and curb its development? The Ministry's outline of business tax stipulates that the maximum rate shall not exceed 2 per mille. It is understandable that the highest tax is levied on consumer goods. Even the unnecessary needs are not taxed at a rate of 5 per mille or 10 per mille, but only at a rate of 2 per mille, which is considered the highest standard. The Ministry is considerate of businesses. We request that your association forward it to the Ministry of Finance to complete the virtuous policy and quickly issue a sub-consultation to the Jiangsu and Zhejiang provincial governments for correction."

▲ Wine Industry: Yesterday, the Wine and Baijiu Industry Association submitted a report to the Ministry of Finance, the Jiangsu Department of Finance, the Shanghai Municipal Government, and a letter to the Municipal Committee for the Study of Tax Regulations on the matter of business tax, stating: "Recently, we read in the newspapers that the Jiangsu Province has promulgated the Provisional Business Tax Regulations, which stipulates that the brewing industry will be taxed at 10 per mille. Does the term "brewing industry" refer to wineries, or does it refer to shops that specialize in selling oil, soy sauce, and wine, which are commonly referred to as "brewing industry"? Both types of shops have already been taxed by the central government for tobacco and alcohol business licenses. Furthermore, wine merchants do not produce wine themselves but transport it from wineries and resell it to retail shops, which specialize in selling oil, soy sauce, and wine. The same goods have already been taxed three times by the central government's license tax. If the brewing industry is included in the local business tax, it would be like adding a bed on top of a bed and collecting taxes repeatedly, which is seriously inconsistent with the Ministry's outline. The burden on merchants at all levels is unbearable. Domestic wines are likely to be greatly affected, which is contrary to the late Premier Sun Yat-sen's emphasis on people's livelihood. The matter concerns the livelihood of wine merchants. Therefore, we specially submit a request to correct and remove the brewing industry listed in the Jiangsu business tax. When formulating the business tax in this city, please exempt the brewing industry to avoid duplication and maintain the Ministry's regulations."

Oil and Bean Cake Industry Requests Exemption from Special Tax

The Shanghai Miscellaneous Grains, Oil, and Bean Cake Trade Association yesterday telegraphed the Nanjing Ministry of Finance, saying: "Respectfully to Minister Song: We recently heard that oil and beans are to be designated as special taxes. Although this has not yet been formally announced, we are quite concerned. We believe that oil and beans are daily necessities and cannot be compared to luxury goods. After the surtax reduction, they should be exempt from taxation. Even if taxes are to be levied, they should be specially reduced. Moreover, the customs already levies export taxes on these items. If they are designated as special taxes, double taxation would be excessive. Merchants are happy about the surtax reduction, but they would be burdened by additional taxes, which is not the government's intention to consider the hardships of businesses. Furthermore, the special tax on cotton yarn only applies to yarn, not to cotton cloth, because they are considered one type of material. Oil comes from beans, and oil and beans are essentially one type, like mother and child. This is similar to the cotton yarn and cloth example, and they should not be taxed separately. As the tax regulations are being discussed, any oversights could easily lead to excessive taxation. If implementation is hindered, and changes are then made, it would damage the government's credibility. Therefore, this association respectfully requests that the Ministry exempt oil and beans from special taxes, in addition to the export taxes already levied by customs. If this is not possible, we request that the cotton yarn and cloth tax example be followed, taxing only one item and not both, and granting a special reduction within that one item to reduce the burden on the people's livelihood and ease the difficulties of businesses. This would be greatly appreciated. Respectfully, Ye Zengming, Chairman of the Shanghai Chinese Merchants Miscellaneous Grains, Oil, and Bean Cake Trade Association, bows."

Yarn Factories Request Transportation of Cotton Stored in Shaanxi and Henan

The Shanghai Chinese Yarn Mill Association telegraphed the Ministry of Industry, Nanjing, yesterday: "Respectfully to Minister of Industry: Since last spring, cotton from Shaanxi and Henan has not been transported out. Reports indicate that there are still 1.4 million dan stored. The cotton harvest in the southeastern provinces has been very poor, and yarn mills rely on foreign cotton. Recently, prices have been extremely high, and there is a shortage of raw materials. We earnestly request that you instruct the authorities in Shaanxi and Henan to find ways to facilitate transportation, and that the railway bureau adds trains to transport the stored cotton out by land. This would allow yarn mills to purchase less foreign cotton, preventing the outflow of money. It would also allow Shaanxi to exchange cotton for food, alleviating famine. This would be a great benefit in several ways. We respectfully request your prompt implementation. Respectfully, the Chinese Yarn Mill Association."

Customs' Combined Collection of Liquor Tax is Difficult to Implement

The Shanghai Chamber of Commerce previously sent a telegram to the Ministry of Finance, requesting that the liquor tax bureau in the Chinese-controlled area be abolished and replaced with a one-time collection by customs to facilitate enforcement, prevent smuggling, and unify tax policies. Yesterday, the Ministry of Finance replied, saying: "This case was previously submitted by the Shanghai Liang Liquor Trade Association, represented by Huang Yuming. The proposed tax rate for liquor is 30% of the value, and 20 yuan per hundred jin for alcohol. This includes all liquor manufactured by foreigners or imitated by Chinese, as well as imported liquor. This liquor tax is a domestic consumption tax and is different from the customs duties on imported liquor and alcohol. The request to have customs collect the tax is difficult to implement. Regarding the prevention of alcohol smuggling, the former provincial Tobacco and Liquor Affairs Bureau also submitted a similar request, which was approved to establish an alcohol inspection station in Shanghai. Now, based on the previous request, we will instruct the Jiangsu Stamp Tax and Liquor Tax Bureau to investigate and deliberate and submit a reply. This reply is for the public association's record and will be sent to the Jiangsu Bureau."

Postal Workers' Demands Reported Yesterday

The Shanghai Postal Workers' Union's request to the central government to maintain the original organization of the union and its demands for a housing subsidy of ten yuan have been repeatedly reported in this newspaper. It is now known that the union has contacted the authorities several times regarding the housing subsidy issue, but there have been no results. Postal workers are extremely angry and seem determined to achieve their goals. The union's petition and notice are recorded below:

▲Petition The Shanghai Postal Workers' Union petitions the Municipal Party Committee to forward to the central government to allow the original organization to be maintained, in order to strengthen the national revolutionary forces and benefit the postal service. The petition states: "Since the union followed the teachings of the late Premier and strived for revolution, it has been nearly seven years. The postal workers have been united and have been devoted to the mission of our party under the leadership of the union. During the Shanghai battle in 1928, they fought bravely against the Zhili-Lu warlords and were honored to sacrifice their lives to assist the progress of the national revolution. Since then, they have moved forward bravely and fearlessly, so that in the period of purification, the communists did not dare to exist in our post office. Looking back at the past work achievements, there is much to be proud of. However, the union does not dare to be complacent. At this time of national unrest, any hesitation would give reactionaries an opportunity to take advantage of the situation. Therefore, in all revolutionary movements under the leadership of our party, the union is determined to lead its postal workers to fight bravely and serve as a model for the people's movement, so that our party's policies can be implemented. No matter how many obstacles there may be, we will not give up. Last year, we opposed the loss of national rights in the Sino-German aviation contract, and our loud appeal shocked society and won public opinion, so that the unequal contract could be revised. Although we were resented by those in charge, we did our best to protect our national rights. As for the postal service itself, the union and its members love it more than their own families. For example, we assisted the government in recovering the postal rights held by foreign countries for more than 30 years. We supported the Premier's belief that the best examination system in China is the postal service's own examination system, and we abolished the document clerks and assistant clerks who had not passed the examination. We opposed the establishment of parallel agencies for the postal savings and remittance business, which wastes public funds. We demanded that those who controlled the post office and embezzled public funds be investigated. All of these efforts were aimed at eliminating all corruption and evil in the postal service, which has been painstakingly operated by our country. Not only is this praised by society as being reasonable and justified, but also by your Ministry and the Executive Committee of the Central Party Department, who have expressed their sympathy and concern. The union is a revolutionary group of postal workers, and it knows the situation best. We have no feelings of good or bad about any event, but only want to protect the postal service and do not want to see it in danger of bankruptcy, which would make us a laughing stock to foreign countries. In summary, the union has been loyal to the national revolution, politics, and the postal service. This has been clear and undeniable. The union hopes to strengthen its unity in the future to serve as a driving force for our party and as a powerful backing. Unexpectedly, news came that the Central Party Department intends to order the reorganization of postal workers' unions throughout the country in accordance with the Trade Union Law. The union was shocked and the public was in an uproar. Although it is still under consideration by the Central Party Department, the union cannot help but speak out. According to the Trade Union Law, the members of the union will be limited to postal workers below the rank of letter carrier. If this is carried out, the union, which has a long and glorious history, will lose its solid

Page 10

solidarity and strength. To put it bluntly, a large revolutionary group of the people will be wiped out. This is probably not what our Central Party Department wants to see. Premier Sun Yat-sen earnestly instructed us to protect labor groups and develop their strength, and our party's previous declarations have also recognized that the people's revolutionary movement not only does not violate the interests of the national revolution, but also increases the strength of the national revolution, so that it can overthrow imperialism, warlords, and all domestic counter-revolutionary forces. Therefore, our party advocates that we must do our best to make the people's movement widespread. From this point of view, the strength of the people is being developed and not destroyed. Undoubtedly, the union does not dare to criticize the Central Party Department's move, but it is afraid that at a time when the revolution has not yet been completely successful, this will weaken the vigorous people's movement in China. At a time when we have not yet entered the period of construction internally and rely heavily on the support of the people externally, it is even more inappropriate to do this. In terms of the postal service, the union has always struggled against corrupt forces. Once these corrupt forces are dissolved, they will run rampant and be even more unscrupulous. The future of the postal service is unthinkable. Even if our postal workers want to protect it, they will not be able to. What the heart feels is dangerous, it is difficult to remain silent. We do not hesitate to risk death to state our case. We hope that you will forward to the Central Party Department and approve the maintenance of the original organization of the union and all postal workers' unions throughout the country, and request that a special trade union law be promulgated as soon as possible in accordance with the original organization of the union. The future of the national revolution and the future of the postal service depend on this. Respectfully submitted, the Shanghai Special Municipal Party Department, the Shanghai Postal Workers' Union, February 11, 1931.

▲Notice Shanghai Postal Workers' Union Notice No. 20 states: "Regarding the resolution of the Second Plenary Representatives' Conference on (1) striving to maintain the original organization of the union and (2) requesting a housing subsidy of ten yuan for all members, the union has been ordered to handle these two cases, and is working hard to implement them and actively strive for them. It has also decided to take steps to specifically handle these two cases. Regarding the first case, in addition to the unanimous support of friendly unions across the country and the joint publication of a declaration, the union has also submitted a petition to the Municipal Party Department to forward to the Central Party Department, stating the reasons and requesting approval to maintain the original organization of postal workers' unions across the country, and requesting the promulgation of a special trade union law as soon as possible in accordance with the original organization of the union. Regarding the second case, we have made every effort to proceed, studied the countermeasures day and night, and contacted the authorities several times, but the authorities have refused on the grounds of lack of sincerity. The public is resentful because, due to the relationship between gold and silver, rents have suddenly increased. This request is a must for our postal workers. We will not stop until we achieve our goal. In summary, public opinion is very sympathetic to these cases and has received support from all sides. However, we hope that all members will wait patiently for a solution during this period, follow all orders from the union, and unite as a backing for negotiations. This is very important. This is hereby notified. Shanghai Postal Workers' Union, February 11, 1931."
