Xiqing Basketball Tournament Ends, McLins Wins Loser's Championship

▲ Defeated East China 29 to 27 Last Night

McLins won every game in the Xiqing Loser's Championship, and eventually won the championship with a full victory. Among the five games, the two games against Qingguang and East China were the closest. The game against East China last night was particularly tense. The overall situation was that McLins was mostly at a disadvantage. However, they rose up in the last ten minutes and finally achieved great success and happily won the championship.

▲ Final Results of Each Team

Team Name Wins Losses Points For Points Against Win Percentage

McLins 5 0 185 147 1.000

Qingguang 4 1 208 141 0.800

East China 3 2 164 153 0.600

Pirates 2 3 160 139 0.400

Laoda 1 4 124 159 0.200

Yeshi 0 5 124 226 0.100

▲ McLins Achieves Great Success

丨East China's Efforts Fall Short丨

Referee Bai Bobo announced the start of the game. East China sent heavy troops. Lu Zhongen exited from the oblique path, Chen Long soared across the sea, and the sound of two goals was very strong. Gu Zhi scored one of McLins' two penalties, immediately tying the score. East China's five tigers fought in a wheel battle, with Chen, Li, Wang, Lu, and Ouyang showing their skills and each scoring one goal, reaching a super peak of 14 to 4. Suddenly, the overall situation tended to be flat. After a long time, McLins gained the upper hand and quickly took down the enemy's fortress. Due to the opponent's tight defense, the gains were limited. East China took the lead with 16 to 12 in the first half. In the sound of the second battle, Huo Shipi suddenly received a pass from Lu and took the opportunity to invade, taking it down in one fell swoop. Lu used a clever plan and took the lead again. Later, Bishuenong and Shatai made contributions one after another, tying the score at 18. Soon, it became 21 and 23. Afterwards, McLins pressed forward and East China followed, and it became 27. In the end, McLins Brown scored a goal and finally took the lead with 29 to 27. It can be said to be extremely lucky.

▲ Qingguang Pirates Benefit

Qingguang's victory over Laoda was actually obtained from a hard battle. At the beginning of the game, the two teams were difficult to distinguish between first and second, and each scored 16 points in the first half. In the second half, Qingguang changed its lineup, and the situation was better. After 19, 21, and 23, Qingguang suddenly rose, and Laoda tried hard to counterattack but failed, and finally lost. As a result, Qingguang won 42 to 28.

The Pirates performed very well. Their offense and defense were impeccable. Yeshi was at a disadvantage and suffered greatly. In the first half, the Pirates scored 29 and Yeshi scored 14. In the second half, the Pirates were as comfortable as they wanted, and their score increased greatly. Yeshi waited to die and was helpless. When the Pirates scored 45 points, Kang Yuefa scored a goal, otherwise the second half would have ended with a duck egg. As a result of the game, the Pirates won 48 to 16. The referees were both Bailey Xin.

Free Talk

Laugh It Off Hai Ke

▲ Owner (running to the electrical company and saying angrily) 丨 I have come twice in a row. I called you to send someone to repair the doorbell on the gate. Why didn't you come?

Electrician 丨 I have also been here twice.

Owner 丨 Nonsense. I didn't see you come here.

Electrician 丨 Yesterday and the day before yesterday. I have been here, but I pressed the doorbell for more than ten minutes and no one came out to open the door. I thought that everyone in your house was completely out on official business, so I returned.

▲ Diner (angrily calling the waiter) 丨 Boy! Boy!

Waiter (coming forward to ask) 丨 What can I do for you, sir?

Diner 丨 This soup is not palatable. Take it away quickly.

Waiter 丨 This soup is very fresh. How can you say it's not palatable?

Diner 丨 This soup is only fit for feeding pigs.

Waiter 丨 That's why I specially brought it up to you.

▲ Young man (asking a beautiful woman at a social event) 丨 Miss, haven't we met before?

Lady 丨 Sir, I have never seen you before.

Young man 丨 I'm afraid Miss has forgotten.

Lady 丨 I have not forgotten. Where did you meet me?

Young man 丨 At Mr. C's spring banquet last week.

Lady 丨 I didn't go.

Young man (blushing) 丨 Ah. Then I didn't go either. I'm afraid it was two other people.

Zhang Huizan's Decisiveness Yang Hua

The Red Army spread to the border. There was no one left. Like Xiang, like E, like Gan. These were the most extreme cases. Zhang Huizan, the commander of the 18th Division of the National Army, died in the Donggu battle. Zhang was a famous general from Hunan. He participated in all the party-state battles in the province. Zhang was involved in all of them. In the National Protection War, Zhang was the commander of the guerrillas in central Hunan. In the aid-E war, Zhang was the brigade commander and commander of the Yangtze River defense. In the bandit suppression war, Zhang was the division commander. During the Northern Expedition of the Founding Army and the Northern Expedition of the Revolutionary Army, Zhang led the division as a partial commander and drove on the battlefield, all of which were defeated. Zhang was especially known for his calculations in the Western Expedition. At that time, Zhang was the deputy army commander of the Second Army. His troops were stationed in Yichang. The army commander was Lu Diping, who was stationed in Nanjing. At that time, the central government was using troops against Tang Shengzhi, which was the so-called "Western Expedition." The Second Army was a central government unit. Tang ordered Wu Shang, Li Pinxian, and He Jian to use the forces of three armies to conspire against the Second Army in order to avoid future troubles. Zhang knew of the plot, so he summoned his generals to a meeting. Everyone thought that the isolated army had no support, so it was better to withdraw from Yichang to western Hunan to wait for the military victory of the central army before planning to respond. Zhang forcefully rejected the crowd's opinions and insisted on going straight to Wuhan, hoping to quickly resolve Tang's troops. He sent messengers to persuade Yang Sen to the west, luring him with Yichang's tax revenue, and persuaded Fang Zhenwu to the north (Fang was stationed in Xiangyang at the time) to work hard for the party-state. Sure enough, the partial army went out in the morning, and Tang's troops were resolved at night.

In Hunan, everyone, whether women or children, knew his name. After being defeated in the aid-E war, Zhang was dismissed from his military post and transferred to the post of police chief of the provincial capital of Hunan. At that time, there was a woman in Changsha named Liu Mazi who specialized in luring women from good families to secretly engage in prostitution. The people of Hunan called it Taiji Ye, or Diaotai. The person in charge was called the Tidiao. Liu Mazi was the only big Tidiao in Changsha. At that time, Zhao Hengti ruled Hunan and made banquets and tours the fashion. Civil officials such as the director of the hall and the secretary, and military officers such as the division commander and the brigade commander, all regarded it as an honor to enter Liu Mazi's door once. Therefore, Liu Mazi's power was overwhelming for a time, and many women from good families were bewitched by her. Even the concubines and young ladies of the dignitaries and celebrities had many who recognized Liu Mazi as their godmother and obeyed Liu Mazi's orders. When Zhang took office, he wanted to arrest Liu Mazi and put her to death. However, because there were so many people she knew, the arrest warrant had not yet been returned, and the guarantee had already arrived. So he first ordered the clerk to record the charges, and personally led the soldiers to Liu Mazi's residence to arrest Liu and take her directly to the execution ground for execution. If he had engaged in interrogation, the guarantors would have come one after another. From then on, Zhang Huizan's name shook the entire Hunan. The people of Changsha still cite it as a topic of conversation today.

Recording the Zhu Chengzhang Memorial Service Sun Choucheng

Mr. Zhu Chengzhang was enthusiastic about public welfare. This time, he was tragically assassinated and died unjustly. Whether they knew him or not, everyone mourned. On the afternoon of the 8th, relatives, friends, and former colleagues held a memorial service for him to express their grief. Choucheng also went to participate. Here is a record of what I saw and felt.

The venue was on the second floor of the YMCA on Sichuan Road. The entrance was surrounded by pine and cypress trees. In the middle was embedded the eight characters "Mr. Zhu Chengzhang Memorial Service." Mr. Zhu was a convert to Christianity, so the ceremonies were different from ordinary ones. There were prayers, scripture readings, and blessings. I went at 2 o'clock and saw four orphans sitting side by side on the right side of the stage. They were all wearing gray cloth robes, white hats, and white shoes, with black gauze wrapped around their arms. On the stage was a half-length Western-style portrait of Mr. Zhu, looking lively and spirited. Above was a horizontal plaque with the inscription "His Spirit Will Last Forever, His Example Will Always Remain." On the side were couplets presented by Minister Song Ziwen and Wang Zhengting: "One Torch Burned the Jade of Bian He, a Tiny Star Fell in the Ninth Heaven," and "Only Grieve for the Unicorn Horn Being Broken, Do Not Compare It with a Feather." Because of the Christian connection, only pine, cypress, and fresh flowers were piled up like mountains. There was no sacrificial table. Twenty potted flowers were placed at the mouth of the stage, and seven wreaths. All the wreaths were embedded with cross shapes. Memorial banners and elegiac couplets were hung all over the four walls. Chairman Kong Xiangxi said when reporting the purpose of the meeting that people must die, but we must ask how the deceased lived before death. The career that Mr. Zhu made can be worthy of God, the country, and society. Then everyone sang a dirge. After the singing, the Westerner Fei Wusheng and Tang Chengxi took the stage to pray, using both Chinese and Western languages. Then Yu Rizhang read a section from the New Testament, Corinthians 1, chapter 15, section 37. When offering flowers, Kong Yongzhi, Yang Dunfu, Zhang Jiafu, Kuang Fuzhuo, and Lin Kanghou all held wreaths in their hands and went to the front of the portrait in a row to bow. On the speech order, it was stipulated that Mayor Zhang and other six people were limited to five minutes each. But as a result, Mayor Zhang spoke for six minutes on behalf of Yu Hongjun, Chen Guangfu spoke for nine minutes, Liu Wang Liming spoke for six minutes, Wang Rutang spoke for eleven minutes on behalf of Yu Rizhang, Bau Nai De (a Westerner) spoke for eight minutes, and Huang Renzhi spoke for twenty minutes. None of them exceeded the limit. Chen Guangfu had the deepest relationship with Mr. Zhu, so he was extremely sad when speaking. The elegiac couplet he presented was also the most poignant. The text said, "The old father is over eighty years old, the children are young, and the wife is weak. The pain is terrible. He abandoned the world after being attacked. He should know that he can close his eyes when he lets go." "We have been in the same boat for fifteen years. We trust each other sincerely. I am sad that the distant guest Yanshan has become an eternal farewell. I can't help but be too sad when I arrive at the funeral." Liu Wang Liming spoke highly of Zhu Jun's kindness to his wife and his care for his husband while concurrently leading his children, saying that this is rare at a time when the family system is being destroyed by borrowing the four words of freedom of love. Huang Renzhi greatly praised Zhu Jun's words of not retaliating against the enemy after the disaster. Then the Shanghai Ya Le Society sang a special dirge. Seven boys and seven girls sang together at the same time, in English. I don't know the meaning, but I just felt like complaining and weeping, which was very tragic. At the end, Pastor Shang Xiuzhong raised his hands and gave a blessing before the meeting adjourned.

Ye Yuhu's Letter to Yang Xiaolou

Mr. Xiaolou, I heard that you have come to Shanghai. Because I have been sick for many days, I have not been able to listen to your elegant performance. I regret it very much. In Beiping, although we often met, we did not have a deep conversation. I know nothing about drama, but because I am interested in literature and art, I am also quite interested in this. I believe that our country's drama today should strive to preserve its truth and characteristics before we can talk about improvement. Otherwise, if the truth is lost first, how can we know its gains and losses? In recent years, in order to keep up with the times, various drama artists have mostly lost their old ways, and the older generation is gradually dying out, and there are few who can succeed them. This is especially the disaster of this way. Your Excellency's art transcends your peers, and there is no enemy today. In Shanghai, which follows the trend, there are still many people who truly appreciate Your Excellency, which is enough to know that fame comes after the fact. There is still a principle in this. However, what I urgently want to tell you is that Your Excellency should be aware that you are a special talent in the Chinese drama industry. For the sake of the Chinese drama industry, you should bear the responsibility of making your own unique art pass on to future generations. Now your age has passed fifty, and your physical strength has a tendency to gradually decline. I don't know if there is anyone among your senior disciples who is sufficient to succeed you. I believe that Your Excellency should pay special attention to selecting those who are of good quality and teachable, and do your best to mold them so that they can glimpse the mystery. In this way, the unique art will not be lost, and the great name will last forever with it. This is far better than leaving property to children and grandchildren. What I saw while sick, I presented frankly. I only hope that you will understand.

Ye Gongchuo, February 8th

The Strange Creature of Xujiacun Village in Yixing, by Jiang Boquan

Five or six li southwest of Heqiao Town in Yixing County, there is a village called Xujiacun Village. Half a li behind the village, there is a large pond, with a circumference of a hundred or so steps. The pond is connected to the outer river, but only by a small, narrow channel. Brambles are planted around the pond, providing resources for fuel. Villagers going to the market by boat must pass by it.

For the past half year, there has been a widespread rumor about a strange creature suddenly appearing in the pond. Villagers going to the market or returning from the market have been traveling together along the paths between the fields, avoiding it from afar. People speak of it with certainty, and within a few days, the rumor spread throughout the village. As a result, those who came to see the spectacle lined the road. Several of my relatives and friends also went to see it. However, no one could name what the creature was, despite the many viewers.

According to nearby residents, there is a large hole in the pond, more than a foot in diameter. There is also a hole of equal size next to the pond where it connects to the water. Initially, every night, a large lamp was seen from afar on the pond, emitting a red light. Upon closer inspection, the light became smaller. Approaching directly to observe it, the light became as small as a firefly, emerging from the opening of the hole. People gradually became suspicious and fearful. They continued to observe it silently for several days and nights. One morning, as the sun was about to rise from the eastern mountains, several villagers lingered by the pond to see what it was. Suddenly, a black dome appeared in the pond, almost level with the surface of the water. Gradually, the dome grew larger. The villagers were terrified and ran away. After a short while, they looked back, and the black dome had expanded to half the pond. When asked, those who had seen it confirmed that their observations were the same. It is said that this creature usually appears in the morning or after meals, especially on sunny days. If there is a lot of noise, it will not be seen.

The creature's mouth is slightly pointed. Some people therefore call it a "dragon-horse." However, no one knows what the creature's head, eyes, or body look like, because the viewers are timid and dare not get close to the pond. Moreover, if they agree to muster courage and go forward, the creature will sink and disappear. Therefore, no one has been able to name what the creature is to this day.

In my estimation, it must be an animal that has lived for many years. There is no such thing as a "monster" in this world. I hope a biologist will go and investigate to clear up the villagers' ignorance and bring it back to exhibit in a museum for people to study. (Unstamped)

Tooth Stone, by Kang An

Tooth stone is not a stone shaped like a tooth, but rather a stone with tooth marks. Its texture is fine and hard, and it is exceptionally beautiful. The locals call it "tooth stone."

Tooth stone is produced in Fuqiu Mountain in the western part of Yiyang, Hunan. Fuqiu Mountain is the second highest mountain in Yiyang. There is an ancient temple on top, inhabited by several monks. The mountain is full of large and small stones, all of which have tooth marks, some more, some less, some beautiful, some ugly. The tooth marks are crisscrossed, some shallow, some deep. The number of teeth varies, and the tooth marks are sometimes wide, sometimes narrow. The locals say they were gnawed by rats or other animals. It is difficult to determine whether there were animals in ancient times that bit stones. The monks say that immortals lived on this mountain in ancient times. They did not cook, but only ate stones to satisfy their hunger. Which of the two explanations is correct? Only geologists can provide an answer.

Since the Meilin Senior Elementary School was opened near the mountain, more and more people have been going to pick up tooth stones. Because of their beauty, they are carved into inkstones, inkwells, or other ornaments, which are very beautiful. Later, through the introduction of a certain gentleman, they were displayed at the Changsha Industrial Exhibition. Appreciators were willing to pay high prices to acquire them, and dozens of pieces were sold out within a week, bringing great profit to the carvers.

Although there are many tooth stones on the mountain now, few are beautiful. The monks in the temple may have collected a few pieces. It is unknown whether there are any still buried underground.

Losses Due to Cold, by Chen Boying

Last year's severe cold, with temperatures only reaching just over ten degrees Fahrenheit, was not only unprecedented in recent years, but also rare since the Guangxu era. As a result, someone lost ten thousand taels of silver. I record it to provide conversation material. There was a Cai Zihuang from Anting, who was once a provincial assemblyman. His family was comfortably well-off. He had a discerning eye and loved to collect. Last autumn, at the home of a certain Mo in the capital, he bought a set of Dong Qichang's calligraphic screens, a copy of the Diamond Sutra in ink, a painting of farming and weaving by a Ming artist, and a spittoon, for which he paid two hundred yuan, which was not enough. When he took them home and examined them carefully, he found that the calligraphy and painting were genuine and worth ten times the price, and the spittoon was actually a Song kiln piece. Song kiln pieces are worth no less than ten thousand taels of silver at current prices. If he waited to resell he could easily get fifty thousand taels. He was overjoyed and wanted to store them carefully. He wanted to display them in the hall, but he was afraid of attracting covetous eyes. He put them in a low place, but he was afraid that the children and servants would be careless and kick them. He put them in a high place, but he was afraid that cats and mice would knock them over. He hesitated for a long time and suddenly became worried about fire. After racking his brains all day, he finally came up with a solution. He bought two large vats and placed the spittoon in one of them, filling it with soil. He thought he had come up with a foolproof plan. At that time, antique dealers got wind of it and asked to buy it. Cai said, "This is a rare treasure and I cannot bear to part with it. But I can show it to you gentlemen to broaden your horizons." So the antique dealers went to his house and asked to see it. Cai opened the vat and took out the spittoon, but one corner was broken off. It turned out that the cold had frozen the water, causing the soil to freeze and break the pottery. Porcelain is valued above all else for its completeness. If it is broken or chipped, it is worthless. Cai then wept, holding the spittoon. Even seven days later, he was still sighing. The spittoon looked like the ones used today, black as lacquer, shining with a strange light. In the middle, at the bulging part, there were four flowering crabapple blossoms around it. The flowers were white as jade, pure and warm. The center of the flowers also depicted landscapes, colored red as a cockscomb and green as emeralds, vivid and lifelike. My friend Mr. Gu saw it with his own eyes. Some say its name was "Zhen."

Epitaph for Yi Junshi (Continued), by Cheng Songwan of Ningxiang

Thus eight years passed. In the year of Gengshen, on the thirtieth day of the eighth month, at the hour of Hai (9-11 PM), he fell ill and died in his residence in the capital. He was born on the fifth day of the ninth month of the year Wuwu in the Xianfeng era, at the hour of Xu (7-9 PM). He was sixty-three years old. With his talent, he bathed in the sun and moon, and his capacity was as vast as the sea and the earth, without limit. His learning encompassed all schools of thought, and he incorporated historical events and evidence into his writing. In an instant, he created myriad things, naturally. At times, his work was like decaying ghosts and burning gods, strange and bizarre. Throughout history, only Li Bai and Su Shi can be compared to him in terms of talent. He once described his life in a poem, saying that the "four souls" he collected were mostly related to national heritage, and the "ten peaks" he visited were Qingcheng, Emei, Zhongnan, Putuo, Kuanglu, Tai, Heng, Dawei, Tiantong, and Luofu, each forming a collection. He also said that his hobbies were mountains and waters, and women, and that if he had mountains and waters, he would forsake women, a hint of spiritual ambition that came from within. In all, he left behind seventy-two volumes of poetry, ten volumes of ci poetry, and twenty-three volumes of historical and miscellaneous writings. Including collections of poems exchanged with others, there are more than sixty kinds. Eighteen or nineteen of these were published. In the last six years, his poetry manuscripts were lost to others and were occasionally seen in newspapers and periodicals. He lived with utmost integrity and had no pretensions to life, death, wealth or nobility. He was trustworthy to his friends and courageous in his actions. Although he was subject to slander and ridicule, he never complained or blamed others. He was persevering, upright, and knew when to stop. He can be said to have sought benevolence. His wife was Liu Jingdong, the granddaughter of a Hunan provincial governor. Their son died young. His second wife was Shen, daughter of Shen Baoxiang, the prefect of Hanyang, from Wuxing. Both sons died young, and both wives were granted the title of Lady. His concubine was Wang, and their sons are Jia Chui, Jia Yue, and Jia Zhu. Zhu died before him. His concubine was Li, and their daughter married a certain grandson of Qu Guoxian of Baojing. He has several granddaughters. On a certain day of a certain month in the year Dingmao, the coffin was returned and buried in the mountains of Hanshou. I had been connected to him by marriage for more than three generations. In the past, he sent me a poem, in which he wrote that if he had an epitaph in future, he would want me to write it. Now, the tomb trees have grown, but there is no inscription. This is my responsibility. In recent years, I have been living in exile on the coast. His younger brother, Shun Yu, and his son, Jia Yue, came one after another, urgently requesting that I fulfill my promise. Therefore, I have examined his deeds and composed this inscription: Valiant in the restoration, illustrious among the Hunan scholars. Beyond the lake, there are three changes, like Su of Dongpo. His father was a teacher, and his administration was benevolent. The wise king called him, calling him "little sage." His talent was benevolent, and he was filial to heaven. Jin Xiong and Tang Chong, he emulates them. He was filial and able to govern, and he was loyal and able to harmonize. He submitted ten thousand words to the throne, but the book was burned and not destroyed. He held the flag on the Yellow River, fighting with one heart against the Red Cliff. The waves could not gnaw at him, his benevolence was like a rock. He traveled ten thousand miles to the wilderness, to Jiaozhi in the south. Proclaiming our emperor's benevolence, he disregarded life and death. The turtle overturned, the pillar broke, there was no end to the return. He redeemed it with poetry, a vast talent. Dry evil, Kun evil, don't bury your pain. Enough, no resentment, share with those who come. Who knows your pain? Only Heaven knows your benevolence. One hut contains all things, changing bodies for a thousand years. Beautiful is that hill, the image is only a ball. I examine the inscription, it will not be erased for ten thousand years.

Commercial News

Financial Gold Prices Plunge Violently

▲ Due to an Abundance of Cash

▲ A Sharp Drop of Twenty-Five Mace Per Tael

▲ Utter Panic Yesterday, on February 11th, the gold market continued its frantic decline. The situation was perilous, volatile, and highly turbulent. In an instant, there were price swings of several to ten taels, an unstoppable trend. People were in a state of utter panic. The difference between the morning and afternoon markets reached sixteen or seventeen taels, making the market unpredictable and chaotic. In the end, there was a drastic drop of more than twenty taels. This was due to the easing of both official and unofficial foreign exchange rates. Official exchange rates had already widened by one and a half points. The selling pressure in the market intensified. In the morning market, companies like Fuchang, Yongfeng, Yuanheng, and Yuansheng all sold off, while Yuanmao, Yongbing, Xingtai, and Kangrun bought in. Overseas silver markets had rebounded. As a result, gold prices plummeted by more than ten taels at the opening. Subsequently, due to a severe shortage of Shanghai banknotes, the sixty-tael mark was briefly broken before drifting erratically, lingering around the sixty-tael level. However, banknote rates seemed to have stabilized. Later in the day, major players like Yuansheng, Yuanmao, Yongfu, and Changfu tended to sell, mainly because the swap date was approaching. Overall, due to the abundance of cash and the need for bulls to pay premiums, many parties took the opportunity to sell off. As a result, market prices continued to decline, eventually breaking through the 750-tael mark, almost without any chance of recovery. Afterwards, bears made some covering purchases, and the market eased slightly, briefly rising above the fifty-tael level. However, with price swings of ten taels, the market seemed to be shrouded in a fog. It was said that foreign exchange rates might continue to rise this morning because it was Wednesday, a day of low trading volume.

▲ Plunge at the Open The March contract opened with a drop of 11.5 taels, priced at 760 taels. This was because the major exchanges rose by 5/16ths, forward rates rose by 1/4, and silver prices rose by 3/4. The European market was very strong, and there was renewed buying interest from the United States, with few sellers. As a result, market sentiment was weak. Private telegraphic transfers increased by 7/8ths yesterday, reaching 59 taels. Subsequently, due to buying by Yuanmao Yong and hedging traders, the price briefly rose to 63.5 taels. Soon after, Yongfeng and Yuancheng sold off, mainly because the exchange rate was weak. Sterling could be settled at 1.25625, and it was known that advance orders had to be priced higher. As a result, there was a sharp drop of 12 taels. When the advance order was announced to be 375 higher for sterling, 75 higher for US dollars, and 4.75 lower for Japanese yen, the price fell to 51.5 taels. Immediately, it rose by another 7 or 8 taels, as March sterling could be purchased at 1.25. Mitsui absorbed April US dollars at 29.4375, and Yucheng, Yongzhi, Feng, Yongfu, and Yu and other companies bought in. At 9:40 AM, the price was 59.5 taels. Later, Fuchang, Yuanheng, Hengxing, Yu, Yongfeng, and other companies sold off, and banks traded short-term US dollars at 29.125, causing the market to decline. By 10:30 AM, the price had fallen to 57 taels, with price swings of 3 or 4 taels in between. Afterwards, Yuanxing, Yongheng, Xingyuan, Yuhe, and other companies chased the market higher. Sterling seemed stable, and Hua Bi absorbed this month at 1.2375. It also traded with Dehua for May at 3.125, causing the gold price to jump by 6 taels. At 11:15 AM, the price was 63 taels. After that, sellers became active, with Yongfeng, Fuchang, Yuanheng, and others competing to sell, suppressing the price by more than 7 taels in half an hour. At 11:45 AM, the price was 55.5 taels. Soon after, it rose by more than 5 taels, with Xinhang and Bingxing buying in, reaching 61 taels. At noon, the price closed at 58.5 taels, and the official price was revised to 833.4 taels, a reduction of 82 to 70 taels.

▲ Irreversible Decline The afternoon market opened at 57.5 taels. Subsequently, due to Yuanmao Yong, Xinhang, Yuancheng, Fuchang, and others aggressively selling off, and due to reports of higher Indian exchange rates, market sentiment was fearful, resulting in a frantic drop of 10 taels. By 2:15 PM, the price had broken through 50 taels, reaching only 47 taels. After that, the price fluctuated without settling. After 3:00 PM, the market suddenly reversed upwards, due to Taikang Run, Zhifeng, Yong Bingxing, and others buying in, driving the price up by 8 or 9 taels. By 4:00 PM, the price was 55.5 taels. After that, selling pressure increased again, causing the market to weaken again. At the closing at 4:30 PM, the price was 51 taels, a drastic drop of 25 taels compared to the previous day. The price later traded around 53 taels. The highest price of the day was 63.5 taels, and the lowest price was 47 taels, a difference of 16.5 taels. The opening price for goods was 62.5 taels, the noon closing price was 58 taels, the afternoon price was 58.5 taels, and the closing price was 53.5 taels. The official price was adjusted to reflect a reduction of a small 76 to 86 taels, then later 82 to 83 taels. The booked price was 54 taels and 59 taels, and the supplementary water price was 54 taels. The afternoon price was 46 taels.

▲ Heavy Selling Pressure In inter-dealer trading, Yongfeng, Yuancheng, Yuanheng, Fuchang, Hengxing Yuan, and Yuan Xingyong were all sellers. Zhifeng Yong, Dadecheng, Yuanmao Yong, Yuantai, and Xinhang had fluctuating positions. Shunli and Wanxing were sellers and buyers at different times. Yuhe, Yucheng Yong, Hengyu, Bingxing, Tong Taichang, and Hengxing were all buyers. In the afternoon, Taikang Run, Bingxing, Hengyu, Wanxing, and Fuli were all buyers. Yuancheng, Yuan Xingyong, Fuchang, Yuanmao Yong, and Xinhang were all sellers. Zhifeng Yong was a seller and then a buyer. Dadecheng had many fluctuations. The Dalian gang bought a total of 1,500 bars and sold over 800 bars. Transactions by the Guangdong gang were scarce.

▲ Holiday Issue The Gold Exchange will be closed on the afternoon of the 16th and on the 17th and 18th of this month. It is expected that all banks and money shops will also be closed on the 17th and 18th, and will resume normal business on the 19th.

The Reuters and Dentsu reports in the morning were uneventful.

Extensive Silver Coin and Foreign Currency Settlements Extend Hours

Commercial customs place great emphasis on the lunar calendar for year-end settlements. Therefore, although there were extensive inflows and outflows during the lunar New Year in the past, there are still more than at the current lunar New Year. Since the government issued an order to allow reconciliation until February 16, the business community no longer regards the national calendar settlement as important. Therefore, it is stipulated that the deadline is in mid-February. Now, the deadline is approaching, and all accounts must be reconciled and finalized. The silver and money industries, which hold the key to Shanghai's commercial finance, are particularly busy. In the past, a notice was issued to extend the ticket collection time by 2 hours, starting on February 10 (the day before yesterday), with a deadline of 4:00 PM. Therefore, it is difficult to normally calculate the detailed amounts of money industry settlements during these few days.

Yarn Market Morning Weak, Evening Strong

The yarn market opened lower in the morning and rose in the afternoon, with an overall firm trend. Bullish sentiment remained strong, and traders were unwilling to let go. In the afternoon, rumors circulated in the market that the increased special margin requirement for buyers might be canceled, leading to a rush of purchases by retail investors. Japanese traders tightened their pulling force on the spot market, further intensifying the upward trend. The yarn market, being closely linked to the cotton market, rebounded due to fundamental difficulties in declining. However, Japanese traders still showed no intention to cover their large short positions. Some claimed that there were ample yarn stocks in Shanghai, and they feared that the yarn market might be weaker than the cotton market if sales remained sluggish next spring.

▲Human Label Trend Still Stable The human label market opened with a decline due to rising U.S. cotton prices and fluctuating exchange rates, causing retail investors to sell and close positions. Prices fell between 3.48 cents and 1.68 dollars. Cotton Market Initially Fell, Then Rose

The cotton market initially fell but then rebounded. However, overseas cotton markets rose, and exchange rates eased slightly, leading some to lean towards short selling. Nevertheless, Japanese traders maintained a strong stance, and their pulling force was tight. Many others echoed this sentiment. Due to the inability to import foreign cotton and the shortage of raw cotton supply, buyers flocked in as soon as prices fell. Sellers appeared like frightened birds, and their strength was weak. In conclusion, the world has not yet reached a cotton famine. If exchange rates can ease, foreign cotton can be imported. The future depends on exchange rate fluctuations.

Grain: Hexia Rice Market Gradually Firms

▲Zhabei Yesterday, the supply of rice from inland areas was scarce, due to the impending closure of rice shops in Shanghai, which discouraged inland merchants from shipping rice to Shanghai. A few sellers were still trying to raise prices, but the inventory in Hexia remained abundant, and buyers were looking to release their holdings. As a result, the market only firmed slightly. High-quality northern japonica rice remained scarce, and wholesale prices were generally better by ten cents, showing a promising trend. Sales of thin indica rice were sluggish, and prices remained unchanged. Arrivals of lamb indica rice were limited, and warehouse owners were hoarding and raising prices, leading to continued price increases. Top-grade rice required 12.20 dollars, while Du Jian and Bu Jian rice remained stable, with normal trading. Reports on the production of rice from Bianyuan Yin Hua were excellent, but local buying interest was weak, and trading volume was limited, so prices barely held steady.

▲Hunan Yesterday, very few boats arrived from various groups. Sales in the local market were not very brisk. Changshu Northern Japonica and Sutongji Northern Japonica initially benefited from the previous day's momentum and firmed up, but then became sluggish due to slow sales. Nevertheless, the price still increased by about half a foot. Southern merchants were eager to sell their thin early rice, but buying interest was still decent, and prices rose by nearly ten cents. Supplies of lamb Du Jian rice remained scarce, and traders and shops made small purchases, leading to a tight market. High-quality white yuan rice was sluggish, while mid-range rice was active, and overall prices remained stable. Daily transactions in various stalls were not sparse.

Book and Newspaper Introduction

Contradiction - Tang Bin

The nationalist literary movement has become a powerful mainstream trend in the Chinese literary world. This is undeniable. Although there are not many nationalist creative novels that appear before us, most of them are rare masterpieces, unlike Proletarian writers who produce a large number of so-called shallow proletarian works, which make us feel that their rudeness is like slogans, with no artistic value at all, disregarding the essence of literature. Therefore, this kind of shallow and rude work cannot have the permanence of literature and will soon decline. The theoretical foundation of nationalist literary theory has been established and consolidated. This is a very obvious fact, because it has a solid foundation in theory. Although the nationalist literary movement has only appeared in the Chinese literary world for a very short time, its creation has been so mature. Although it cannot be said to have reached the highest peak of art, its technology is different from that of some shallow and rude proletarian works, and readers with considerable appreciation ability can probably understand this.

Pioneer Monthly is a powerful periodical of nationalist literature. It has now published three issues, and each issue is very rich in content. In addition to publishing a large number of theoretical and critical articles, it is particularly inclined to nationalist literary creation. Although it is not a large amount in quantity, we admire it in quality, because each article is the author's carefully crafted work, which shows the strictness of the editor in selecting creations.

Here, we want to recommend Li Zanhua's works as the most skilled in terms of technology. The article "Contradiction" published in this issue is a rare work in the domestic creative world. In form, it is not as rude as proletarian works, and in words, it is not as shallow, but it contains national . We can see the greatness of nationalist literary creation.

The content of the story "Contradiction" is very simple. It is about Yan Qiao, a clerk in a foreigner's office, being questioned by the pig-like supervisor for secretly forming a association. Young people's temperament is inherently strong, but for the sake of livelihood, they have to submit to the claws of foreigners. Here, the author wants to express that there are contradictions everywhere in the current world. With this kind of inextricable contradiction, people can feel the need for revolution. This is a very obvious fact.

The author's writing is very skilled. In the organization of each word and sentence, we can see his efforts in deliberation, so we always feel that what the author writes contains contradictory will. This is something that people without sufficient literary cultivation cannot do. At the beginning of this article, the author powerfully expresses:

The air in the office is always so dull and so thick, as if it is a solidified fog. This fog seems to be separated from the outside world into two worlds. It is so violent that he rushes in and retreats quickly...

Such sentences are so skillful, and such meaning is so deep. Readers can always understand it. I think that it is definitely not something that ordinary creations can express so powerfully. It is even more beyond the reach of proletarian works.

Then, it is written that the pig-like person is so solemn and uses a heavy attitude towards lower-level employees such as Yan Qiao. When he walks into the office staggeringly and flips through the thin records, some are signed immediately, but some make him frown and throw them aside. At this time, the employees inevitably have a burst of panic and unease, and their anxious hearts feel that his face is so heavy and they are so small. Here, we can understand that a person's psychology has contradictory phenomena floating and sinking, and at the same time, there are contradictions everywhere in the current world. This pig-like person calls Yan Qiao to his room to question him. Here, Yan Qiao walks into the world of imagination from the flat ground.

Yan Qiao feels restrained and unnatural in the world of imagination. He doesn't know where to put his body. The white, fat, pig-like person points to the chair in front of him for him to sit on. He bends his waist and sits down, understanding that this world belongs to others. The author's expression is so powerful and light, making us feel angry. Why don't we stand up and make a revolution for our Chinese nation? At the same time, the author is instilling a large amount of upward consciousness. This suggestive power is full of literary factors. If a proletarian writer were to describe it, it would definitely turn into a rude shout, promoting some revolutionary doctrine for a certain class.

Of course, we have no freedom when we eat under the control of foreigners. Therefore, we feel that the Chinese nation is suffering from foreign oppression very seriously. Here, the author reveals it in a very light style, for example:

"Freedom? You go be free. The foreign manager wants to fire people yesterday, why don't you understand?"

It's better to be fired. It's not the way to go on like this with a dying will. He intends to answer with such words, but in this other world, the courage of the young man disappears.

This, the author clearly tells us that we cannot get freedom under the control of foreigners, but for various reasons, we dare not resist, and we also understand that this is the weakness of young people. This has already become a contradiction. Later, the author's expression is even more powerful, encouraging us to fight for the Chinese nation:

He thought that he himself was a young man who had gone through the revolutionary upsurge. He knew that it was a big mistake to break into such a cage. In the past two years, his courage has been much depressed. Why should I jump out of our era? Why can I abandon the life and death of the nation and spend these two years of muddled life? Watching the courage gradually turn into powder under the grind of life, watching everything of the young people disappear, can I be willing to do this?

Really, these are extremely meaningful words. If young people have such reflections, our Chinese nation will definitely flourish soon. This is an indestructible fact. The highest hope is just to be like that pig-like person, smiling at foreigners and staring at his own people. A Chinese puts his hope on this, which is really the most hopeless and too pitiful. This is another kind of artistic technique, which can also arouse our anger. Young people should cheer up and work hard for our Chinese nation. A great literary work must have ups and downs. Ordinary descriptions cannot express the value of art. Even so, the reader will feel a monotonous meaning. Then, the author directly depicts it: "He thought of that pig-like person, his eyes were about to shoot out fire. He had endured his insults for two years, and he had lost his entire freedom under his restraints. The pig-like person taught him not to be a person, taught him to endure and willingly be a slave, and took thirty-six yuan from his hand every month, as if he had sold everything about himself. However, he was resold to others. This kind of fact, those who work under the control of foreigners can think of it, but cannot express this situation vividly, especially in literary works. From this, we can see that the author's description of the psychology of young people has reached a high level. His analysis of women's psychology, Yan Qiao's wife, is even more realistic and vivid. Due to space limitations, readers can only appreciate its true meaning for themselves.

The entire structure is extremely compact, with almost no branches that can be cut. This is the author's ability to cut. In art, this creation has undoubtedly reached a mature side. Nationalist literary creation has only appeared in the Chinese literary world for a very short time, and it has given us such great achievements. It is really commendable. Compared with the shallow and rude proletarian works, the distance is really like the difference between heaven and earth. This is the fact before us. Nationalist literary works are not produced in large quantities like so-called proletarian works, so the skill of its technique is also a major reason.

Youth Garden

Before and After Graduation 君平

"Haha, this semester can finally end!"

Bin held a course selection form, ran back from the registrar's office, and said triumphantly,

"What's up, Lao Mi, are you graduating in the winter break?"

"Casually, graduating in three and a half years, saving a semester."

Bin's face was full of smiles, his feet tapping the floor, and all the muscles in his body vibrated.

Originally, Bin still had a year before graduation because he was still short twenty-six credits. According to the school's current regulations, he could only take twenty-two credits in a semester. This time, it was really beyond Bin's own expectations. After telling the provost all kinds of difficulties, the provost actually wrote the words "Special Permission" on his course selection form. Thus, Bin's graduation deadline was also shortened by half a year under the provost's pen.

In Bin's own view, this was indeed a piece of good fortune.

Two months of time passed. Bin saw the notice of the graduate examination period on the president's bulletin board. So, he intensified his work on the graduation thesis, which was already more than half done. After the electric lights went out at night, he raised the tip of his pen under the faint candlelight and scribbled on the paper. He still got up very early in the morning, washed his face, and then continued to scribble with that old-fashioned Parker fountain pen.

With great difficulty, the graduation thesis was completed. A smile often appeared on Bin's face, as if the difficult hurdle before graduation had been overcome, and the future was full of hope. Bin thought that life after graduation would be very different from today.

The next morning, Bin got up, put on his overcoat, and put on his hat, and set off for a photo studio. After arriving at the photo studio, Bin changed into a bachelor's gown, put on a bachelor's cap, and struck a perfect pose, asking the shop assistant to take several photos. At this time, Bin stood in front of the mirror looking at his own image. An unnamed joy suddenly surged from his heart.

A few days later, the apprentice from the photo studio delivered the photos. Bin took them out and looked at them, feeling that everything was okay, but the spirit was a little lacking. This could only be said to be a flaw in the ointment, so there was no need to pursue it. Thus, a layer of amiable smile floated on his face again.

"I should first give one to my most intimate friend,"

Bin sat at his desk thinking, his eyes fixed on the photos in his hand, his face floating with two dimples of wanting to drop a laugh.

"No, I should first pick one from inside to give to my lover," Bin continued thinking,

"Lao Zhang, do you want me to give you one?" Bin's gaze flashed towards me, his face slightly showing a hint of joy, "Don't need it, the photograph of Bachelor Mi."

"Haha, ..............."

Bin laughed involuntarily when he heard me call him "Bachelor Mi."

The day of the graduation examination arrived. Bin walked slowly into the classroom every day with the sound of the bell, and answered casually in the classroom, as if the score had nothing to do with him. At the same time, his behavior seemed somewhat abnormal, and the dimples on his face gradually disappeared.

After the exam, Bin's complexion was different from before the exam. At this time, Bin's face was only filled with depression and annoyance.

Perhaps Bin has already tasted the fun of graduating. In this time of overstaffing, the problem of the way out after graduation is really not easy to solve. Look, how many unemployed college students are there in China now? If we investigate it in detail, this number will really scare us.

Three weeks had passed, and Bin's livelihood problem was still not solved. Yes, everyone has to eat. This, for Bin's future, naturally added a layer of tragic expression to his round face.

One afternoon, Bin received a notice from the secretariat, saying that the president wanted him to go to his house tomorrow morning to talk. Bin thought that he had written a letter to the president a week ago. This time, calling him to talk may be related to his problem of finding a way out. In an instant, he thought again that the president had helped several graduating students find a way out not long ago, and they all have things to do now. Yes, his own problem of finding a way out will definitely be solved in the sound of this conversation. Bin carefully folded the note and put it in his wallet, a slight hint of joy appearing on his face.

The next day, Bin got up especially early, washed his face, and stepped out of the door to head towards the president's house.

When he arrived at the president's house, the president had not yet gotten up. Bin sat in the living room for more than two hours before he saw the president walk out of the room.

"Is that Mi Bin? You came very early," the president said,

"What time did the secretariat's note arrive?" the president continued to ask,

"Yesterday afternoon,"

"At the current time, finding things is really difficult. I wrote three or four letters of introduction for you, but none of them worked out,"

"............" After hearing what the president said just now, Bin felt like a basin of cold water had been poured on him, and the passion that filled his heart completely disappeared.

"Please ask the president to find a way again," After a while, Bin said with a pleading attitude,

"Yes, I will pay attention to it for you all the time,"

Talking to this point, Bin said goodbye to the president and came out. After hesitating on the road for a while, he finally hailed a rickshaw and returned to the school.

In the room, Bin kept his mouth tightly closed and did not speak. "Lao Mi, how was the result of the conversation?" After a while, I asked him, succumbing to curiosity.

"I won't tell you for the time being," Bin said a little bit frustrated, not wanting to answer.

Then, the room fell silent.

"Your life is really interesting, heaven doesn't care, earth doesn't care," After a while, Bin said as he walked, as if he was thinking about something,

"Where is it interesting, graduating is the interesting part."

"Graduating is interesting, yes, that's what people who haven't tasted the taste of graduation say."

"Then, is graduating painful?"

"At least it's not happy. I feel that, especially graduating from university is even more painful."

"Then, at the beginning of the semester, why did you rush to graduate?"

"That was my fantasy before graduation. At that time, I thought that graduating was happy, just like you do now."

…………………………………

Bin and I argued for a while, and finally he won.

Finally, Bin said that the purpose of studying is to serve the society, but the society does not give us the opportunity to serve, so there is only pain after graduation. In fact, I have already understood this truth, but I do not believe that the society is absolutely not giving us the opportunity to serve.

But the fact is placed in front of us, the society is indeed rejecting a group of students who have just come out of university.

It has been more than two months since Bin graduated, and he is still unemployed.

A Pair of Youths Man Yin

"Are you leaving tomorrow, Wang?"

"Yes, I'm leaving this place tomorrow, but going to Beijing is still a story for later, because Mr. Li asked me to wait at his house for two days and go with him,"

"Then, I'll come to the North Railway Station to see you off the day after tomorrow, okay?"

"Don't bother, save the trouble,"

"What bothering, this is what should be done, where else can we vagrants find sympathy except in asking each other's friends?" His words seemed to arouse Wang's sadness.

"Ah..." Wang sighed a long breath,

He himself fell even deeper into the sad scene of parting, as if there were infinite sorrows and troubles blocking his heart, making him feel uncomfortable.

There was a temporary silence in the room.

The sound of car bells on the road, the sound of loudspeakers and drums in the shops to attract customers, and countless city voices were really a chaotic mess. Slowly, through the transmission of air, they resounded in the room where they lived.

At this time, Wang was bowing his head doing his work, packing his luggage. As for him, in the name of organizing books for Wang, he roughly read the contents of those books like a horse watching flowers. However, his heart had never noticed a single word in the books. He listened to the noisy sounds on the road, like sobbing, like crying, like wailing, like groaning, rising and falling like waves. He couldn't help but feel a great sense of disgust.

In fact, rather than saying that the noise on the road was annoying, it was more appropriate to say that the lonely, boring, and sorrowful atmosphere in the room was suffocating and making people uncomfortable, because the former was lively and energetic, while the latter was gloomy and dead-like melancholy.

Yes, dead-like melancholy. The ancients said that parting in life is the most unbearable time. Aren't they in the time of parting in life at this moment?

He threw the books he was organizing in his hand onto the table, stood up abruptly, and said angrily,

"It's really annoying, these miscellaneous sounds,"

He walked to the window and pushed the unclosed window door hard, meaning to complain about why it didn't isolate the noisy sounds on the road, but let them invade people's hearts in the room. However, the window door stubbornly opened instead because of the resistance. Thus, "ding-dong" "rumbling" all the sounds on the road rushed to knock on his eardrums, and all the "colors" of red and green in the city also penetrated into his eyes. He then stood in front of the window and looked out.

The sky seemed to be as melancholy as his mood. The sun hid behind the clouds, and a gust of cold wind blew in his face. He felt that it was drizzling in the air. Looking down on the road, it was still red and green, pairs of pairs, like ten thousand arrows, wriggling trams, like long snakes, flying cars, like running tigers, and these ten thousand arrows, long snakes, and running tigers seemed to unite to attack him. The chaotic sounds on the road were the sound of the attack, finally making his heart ache and feel uncomfortable.

He stood in front of the window in a daze, thinking about the past. He was from Jiang province. After graduating from a certain middle school in Jiang province, he worked in a newspaper office. This occupation was quite in line with his interests, because he liked literature and thought that there would be plenty of writing opportunities in the newspaper office. He couldn't help but be happy. In terms of life, an income of fifty yuan of ocean per month was also enough to spend. However, he finally quit this good job. Here, we can't blame him for his bad temper, or say that he "doesn't know the times." Originally, he was a young man, a young man with blood, who couldn't stand the officials in the newspaper office putting on airs and hating the current reviews and editorials written by those editors who catered to the trend. He felt that this environment was not suitable for him, because if you want to continue to do it for a long time, you have to mess with them. What playing cards, treating guests, and prostitute... are all indispensable social activities in the modern officialdom.

How can this work? If I learn these tricks, then will I still become a young man? Moreover, am I willing to bury my future in such a dirty environment?

No, no, I want to leave this place, leave this life that is very well-off, but the environment is very bad, reporter, life, for my career, for my future,

Go, go to the seaport,

Since he started working in the newspaper office, he felt that his knowledge was not enough, and it was necessary to study again. His impoverished family could not provide his tuition fees. He often thought about going to the seaport to work and study at the same time, and he knew that the seaport was the birthplace of modern culture, gathering many literati and scholars. He dreamed that in such a high-level cultural environment, he would definitely be able to get the knowledge, ability, and experience he wanted. He also worried about the livelihood problem, but he thought that it was nothing. There are many factories in the seaport. As long as you can endure hardship, if you can't find a suitable job, you can work in the factory. He firmly believed that a young man, a pure, faithful, and ambitious young man, would never be abandoned by the society. "If you can't sell brainpower, then sell physical strength," he often said.

So he came to the seaport.

Before setting off in Jiangbu, he also returned to his hometown, which was three hundred miles away from Jiangbu, to say goodbye to his old parents, saying that their son was going on a long journey.

"A friend in the seaport has found a good position for you, is that right?" The father, who was over fifty years old and often exhorted to earn money to support the family, asked, because he was studying, and the family still owed hundreds of dollars in debt.

"Yes, father, a friend in the seaport wrote a letter asking me to go," he lied to his father.

"In my opinion, it's best not to go, son, the seaport is too far away, and the age is not good. It's better to work in the newspaper office in this province. The place is closer, and people are also familiar with it. It's better to slowly seek development in the future," his loving mother said,

"You women don't know what to do," the father said, "A man has ambition in all directions, and the world is his home. As long as a friend in the seaport asks him to go, why not go? What are you doing by just guarding the local area?" Although the parents were comforting each other like this, when it came time to part with their son, he said, "Dad, Mom, I'm leaving,"

"Okay, you go, be careful on the road," it was his father's trembling voice,

"Don't forget your home, son, write a letter back when you get there, so that your mother won't worry," his mother shed tears,

He deeply understood the parents' love for their son, which cannot be described in words.

With the development of transportation in the 20th century, a journey of more than three thousand miles only takes three days by ship. He came to the seaport from Jiangbu. When he first arrived in the seaport, he was quite surprised. A naive child from the countryside suddenly mixed into this second Paris in the East seaport. The great warship, the towering foreign houses, the wide roads, the bustling streets, and the beautiful women with colorful dresses, he couldn't help but spread out the stuffy air that had been accumulated in Jiangbu for a long time, and tried his best to find the source of his life and pursue his ultimate destination in the embrace of this big city. He wants to work hard, he wants to move forward, he wants to shake up his spirit and walk on the road of life with big strides...

......Time flew by for three months. What was the result of his efforts to move forward? Besides disappointment, grinding, what he got was nothing but insults, ridicule, poverty, freezing and starvation...... At first, he went to apply for advertisements on newspapers that were recruiting staff and was rejected. He wanted to sell articles and write manuscripts, but he was either ignored by the editors, or "This journal is suspended, and your manuscript will be returned." Finally, he went to the factory to find work, but he was stubbornly designated by the factory staff as a suspected worker movement person. "Is this how society treats a young man so cruelly?" He often sighed and hated, and it was even more common to fall into the abyss of disappointment and cry sadly. His brain was originally a bit neurotic, and even then he lost the ability to organize and self-control, sometimes crying, sometimes laughing, causing the girls of the second landlord to laugh at him, saying that he was "crazy." Of course, he could no longer concentrate on reading and working hard to write. All day long, he just curled up in a small booth and slept. When his mind was hot, he ran to the road. One day, two days, a week, ...... that's how it passed. His body was not very strong to begin with, and recently, because of dietary imbalances, or to put it bluntly, starvation, he became thin and weak. Now he understands that all the prosperity and liveliness of the seaport are of no benefit to a poor, unfamiliar vagrant, except to make you angry, hate, curse, and even cry sadly......

If he were forced to say what the benefits of coming to the seaport for three months were, then he could not help but mention Mr. Kuang, as well as Wang, whom he met through Mr. Kuang's introduction, the Wang who was about to separate.

Mr. Kuang is a famous socialite in the seaport, who has helped him a lot in terms of spirit and material. This, in Mr. Kuang
